Europe Will Convene a Conference of Four Powers

MacDonald May Meet with Hitler

Reactions of Various Countries to the British Prime Minister's Diplomatic Remarks

National News, Berlin, 25th – The German political circles welcome British Prime Minister MacDonald's speech in the House of Commons advocating the revision of the peace treaty. Newspapers expect that Britain and Germany will exchange views on the agreement proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and endorsed by MacDonald, and although its nature is difficult to predict, it is believed that a meeting between the British Prime Minister and the German Chancellor is not impossible. However, it is heard that preliminary negotiations will still be handled by ordinary diplomatic organs, and direct talks will be held after the thorns have been cleared, and then a four-power conference will be convened.

Reuters, Berlin, 24th – German political circles commented on Prime Minister MacDonald's speech in the House of Commons yesterday, calling it "very calm" and proving that France has rejected the four-power agreement proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. Political observers, after reading MacDonald's speech, feel that its tone is very different from the optimism expressed by MacDonald in Rome.

Reuters, Paris, 24th – French newspapers mostly criticized British Prime Minister MacDonald's statement in the House of Commons today on the results of his visit to Geneva, Rome, and Paris. For example, the Paris Echo said, "Encouraging retaliation will only encourage the dictatorships of Hitler and Mussolini to run rampant." French newspapers are deeply afraid that the steps taken by Britain and Italy will lead to the revision of the peace treaty, and French newspapers insist that France is not yet prepared for this. British Conservative member Churchill's statement that diplomatic affairs should be handled by ordinary diplomatic organs is very much opposed to MacDonald's continental negotiations, and France has greatly praised it.

Airplane Adventure at the Summit of the World

British Aviator to Depart from India Tomorrow

(National News, New Delhi, 25th) The Everest Aerial Exploration Team announced today that it will depart by plane on Monday to explore the summit of the world. It is expected that it will conquer the world's highest peak after three hours of flight. Everest is the highest peak in the Himalayas. This is the third aerial attempt. The peak is 28,000 feet high, and the aircraft must be at least 35,000 feet high to prevent various unexpected dangers.

Havas, Yugoslav Capital, 24th – British Prime Minister MacDonald's speech to the House of Commons yesterday shocked people here. In general, for the Little Entente countries, there is no such thing as revising the treaty, and Article 10 of the League of Nations Covenant guarantees the territorial integrity of the signatory countries. It is also said that MacDonald's declarations in Rome, Paris, and London are quite different. What is MacDonald's true intention? It is hoped that he can say it clearly to avoid public confusion.

Reuters, Warsaw, 24th – The newly appointed Polish Ambassador to Italy, Botocki, has resigned today. It is said that Botocki's move is against the policy decided by the two countries during British Prime Minister MacDonald's talks with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini at the end of last week.

Disarmament Conference Begins Discussion

The New MacDonald Plan

Little Entente Expresses Acceptance in Principle

Turkey Also Demands Equality of Armaments

Havas, Geneva, 25th – The General Commission of the Disarmament Conference held a full-day meeting to discuss the procedural issues, but the opinions of all parties have not yet been determined. It is not known whether the General Commission will adjourn immediately or continue to review the MacDonald Plan chapter by chapter. Semi-official sources argue that the General Commission can conclude the debate and use the British Plan as the basis for a draft disarmament convention, but before discussing the detailed articles, there must be more detailed research among the governments of various countries, which is also recognized by official sources.

National News, Geneva, 25th – The general debate on British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament plan by the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference is expected to be extended to Tuesday next week. According to the current schedule, the committee will begin to discuss the details of the plan, and it may be completed before Easter. The committee's sudden acceleration of work is due to the proposal of Chairman Henderson. Henderson initially opposed rapid progress, believing that it was better to wait until the political atmosphere was slightly clearer and to pay particular attention to British Prime Minister MacDonald and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's efforts to promote the four-power understanding. However, Henderson's recent proposal is believed to be unable to benefit the British plan, because in the current situation, the British plan will eventually be shelved, like previous plans. It can be seen from the first day of debate that there was no real result, but only showed the contradictions in the opinions of the great powers.

Havas, Geneva, 24th – This afternoon, the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference began to discuss the disarmament plan proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu spoke on behalf of the Little Entente countries, saying that the British plan could be used as a basis for discussion, that some of its articles could be recognized, that others needed to be revised, and that there were some shortcomings that needed to be supplemented. Swiss representative Motta said that the claims of the various countries were mutually different, and the British plan was nothing more than a compromise solution and left room for improvement. Representatives from the Netherlands, Hungary, and Turkey all praised the efforts of the British government, saying that its plan could give people new hope and was a significant advance. The Turkish representative mentioned the talks in Rome and Paris, saying that the Turkish government only learned about these matters from the newspapers, which was very strange, but that if effective decisions were to be taken, the entire body of the Disarmament Conference must reach a unanimous compromise. The Turkish representative also asked the General Commission whether, since the provisions of some treaties concerning land, sea, and air forces were to be abolished, the provisions of the Treaty of Lausanne concerning the demilitarization of the Bosphorus Strait of Turkey should be dealt with in the same way. After the representatives of Norway and Denmark spoke, the Polish representative took the floor, raising only some questions concerning procedures, but reserving the right to speak in the general discussion. The General Commission is scheduled to continue the discussion tomorrow morning.

Havas, Geneva, 24th – This afternoon, British Foreign Secretary Simon arrived here by plane and immediately attended the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference. When the meeting was convened, the Turkish representative spoke, demanding that the principle of equality of armaments be extended to the demilitarized zone of the Bosphorus Strait. As a result, a new element was added to the discussion. It is expected that the general discussion will continue until Monday evening or Tuesday, after which the General Commission will decide whether to continue discussing the British plan chapter by chapter without interruption, or whether to postpone the discussion until after Easter. The issue of postponing various technical works of the Disarmament Conference is also likely to be raised at that time. (Note: The Treaty of Lausanne, signed by Turkey and the great powers in 1922, stipulates that demilitarized zones should be established on both sides of the Bosphorus Strait, the Dardanelles Strait, and certain islands.)

Reuters, London, 24th – British Foreign Secretary Simon flew from London to Geneva today to attend the discussion of the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference on the draft agreement proposed by the British Prime Minister last week. Because he was delayed on the way between Lyon and Geneva, Simon did not arrive at the meeting until after it had begun. The representative of the Little Entente, Titulescu, first began the debate on the convention, saying that the three Little Entente countries he represented were prepared to accept the British proposal as a basis for discussion, but reserved the right to propose amendments in the future. Swiss representative Motta also held the same attitude, saying that the British Prime Minister's plan had preserved the Disarmament Conference. Representatives from Norway, Turkey, and other countries spoke one after another, criticizing several of the proposed conventions. Norwegian representative Lange said that restrictions on the budget, supervision of arms manufacturing, the definition of aggression, and punishments for aggressor countries were all necessary provisions, but that this convention did not mention a single word, which was regrettable. Debate must continue tomorrow, and the debate will probably end on Tuesday.

China United Press, Tokyo, 25th – Because the new disarmament proposal put forward by British Prime Minister MacDonald has a great bearing on Japan, a joint meeting of the important departments of the Army, Navy, and Foreign Affairs was convened at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 10:00 this morning to carefully deal with it and review the final instructions. After completion, the Japanese delegation in Geneva was immediately instructed by telegram to act accordingly.

Reuters, Tokyo, 25th – Instructions will be sent to the Japanese delegation in Geneva, stating the attitude of the Japanese government towards the British disarmament plan. The statement (1) cannot recognize those who violate the Pact of Paris (Kellogg-Briand Pact) as actual aggressors; (2) cannot recognize the plan regarding the restriction of the army, because the military strength of Japan's neighbors, China and Russia, is currently unknown; (3) cannot recognize the suggestion for naval restriction, the attitude will be decided after the discussion of suggestion proposed by Japan on December 10th last year; (4) cannot recognize the plan for the restriction of the air force, because the development of Japanese aviation affairs is still comparatively backward.

Havas, Paris, 24th – Foreign Minister Pengu met with diplomatic reporters from the press today. Pengu said, "Based on my experience in Geneva for the past eight years, I am convinced that no matter whether political or economic conferences are held internationally, it is difficult to succeed without prior diplomatic preparation. Open discussions at international conference tables can only be the final scene of the work between the foreign ministries and embassies of various countries. To cite two examples, the difficulties encountered by the Disarmament Conference for the past year are only due to insufficient preparation and disputes between the opinions of various countries. If ways are sought to eliminate them in advance, the conference will be facilitated. Conversely, the reason why the Locarno Treaty was successful was because of the long preparation beforehand," and so on.

President Madison Capsizes

Reuters, Seattle, 24th – The 14,000-ton mail ship President Madison suddenly capsized here at her mooring today. The ship is filled with water, and it is now believed that three crew members have failed to escape.

Current Affairs Commentary

From North to South Darkens

Japan's invasion of Northeast China encompassed four provinces, fully unleashing its military force to invade and expand territory, in order to conceal its internal ugliness and divert its people's domestic anger outward. In fact, Japan, calling itself a military nation, having utilized the old customs of feudal tradition, the so-called Bushido spirit, and further importing German militarism, the majority of Japanese people have been nurtured within this framework for the sixty years since the Meiji Restoration. The "national policy of one war every ten years" is especially regarded as a guideline by the army and navy. However, after the capitalist system has grown and matured excessively, the tools used for war and the actual underlying strength must be based on the nation's wealth and natural resources, and then a three-dimensional battle can be grasped. Japan's total national wealth is only 1.022 billion yen (only one-sixth of that of the United States), and the reserves of coal and iron are extremely scarce, with even rarer reserves of oil. Once an international war is provoked and maritime navigation is blockaded, it will be trapped in a predicament even before the outcome on the battlefield is decided. Therefore, taking advantage of our country's inadequate strength and lax national defense, it launched a sudden invasion of the Northeast and then trampled over Jehol, so that the deficiency in coal and iron could be obtained from the virgin land of the four northeastern provinces.

The militaristic Japan is not satisfied with exclusively swallowing the four northeastern provinces. If the countries still want to restore the international balance in the East and insist on the truly open-door policy in Manchuria, then the principle of the League of Nations has been discussed to the fullest extent. Japan's brutal advancement has not ceased, and thus a storm has suddenly arisen. The trusteeship of the three island groups of Mariana, Caroline, and Marshall north of the equator has become a problem due to Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations. According to international common practice, since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, the territories entrusted to it by the League of Nations should naturally be returned without any doubt. However, Japan has made many evasive arguments on this point. Its military believes that:

"...Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations does not解除 the entrusted governance of the South Seas... Moreover, in fact, (the South Seas islands) are the lifeline of Japan's national defense, so they must be firmly maintained..."

"...Regarding the issue of entrusted governance (of the two South Seas island groups), although there are various arguments from the perspective of international law, the most appropriate view now is that the sovereignty of the entrusted territory should belong to the five major Allied Powers. In other words, the sovereignty of the entrusted territory does not belong to the League of Nations. Moreover, my (Japan's) entrusted territory is a C-type territory, so it should be a part of Japanese territory and can be used for all kinds of facilities. Therefore, even after our country (Japan) withdraws from the League of Nations, there is absolutely no need to return it to the League of Nations, but only to submit an annual report on governance to the League of Nations..."

The so-called "national defense" and the so-called "lifeline" have actually been extended from north to south to the three island groups north of the equator. At the beginning of the conclusion of the Treaty of Versailles, the disposition of Germany's old colonies was handed over to the Allied Powers for trusteeship, and this trusteeship should be a peaceful trusteeship, which must not allow the trustee country to establish military defenses or use them as naval military fortresses for its own interests. However, since Japan has been entrusted with the governance of the three South Seas island groups, it has secretly built fortresses, and its construction costs have exceeded 15 million yen. From the Ogasawara Islands along the Mariana Islands to Palau, it forms an arc. What is the intention behind this? It goes without saying that it is aimed at the United States. The United States wants to actively develop the Far East, but its foundation is weak. The Philippines are isolated 6,000 nautical miles away. Although Hawaii is in the middle to provide assistance, how can the 4,000-mile sea voyage be expected to maintain close communication?

The islands of "Guam" and "Yap" are indeed important routes for communication between the United States and the Philippines. If the construction of the "Guam" fortress is completed, the naval base will be more convenient than Manila. However, restricted by the Washington Treaty and limited by the current financial resources of the United States, it has to be temporarily shelved. Therefore, Japan, which disregards international treaties and good faith, can secretly carry out its military construction. If a change occurs in the Pacific, it can rely on its geographical advantage to cut off the connection between the United States and the Philippines in a short period of time, so that our country will be entirely under its threat. Even if the United States has a strong navy and wants to fly over more than 5,000 miles of the Pacific Ocean to attack Yokosuka and other support points, it is feared that it will inevitably fall into the same fate as the Baltic Fleet in the era of the Russo-Japanese War.

Therefore, Japanese militarists took advantage of the international turmoil and uncertainty, the unrest in Europe, the unabated financial panic in the United States, and our country's inability to fight, to seize by trickery and turn peaceful trusteeship into armed rule, and have clearly stated that they will never let go, even recognizing the three island groups north of the South Seas equator as the lifeline of their national defense. Although the United States initially proposed exchange conditions at the beginning of the trusteeship, it can be said to have held the power of "consultant" in the treaty. In today's era of surging nationalism in Germany, it is naturally impossible not to intervene, but the road is long and the power is weak, which is not as convenient as the situation of Japanese imperialism. However, the control of the Pacific is a matter of life and death for the United States of America, and it is difficult to sit idly by and watch the development of the situation in the future. The dispute between Japan and the United States is more serious than the dispute between Japan and Germany, and it is feared that it cannot be resolved by past protests and debates.

Japan will tomorrow

Announce its Withdrawal from the League of Nations

(Tokyo) The Japanese Privy Council will hold a plenary meeting at 10:00 a.m. on the 27th in the Imperial Palace to review the proposal to withdraw from the League of Nations. Regarding the handling of this proposal, after the meeting on the 22nd, the advisors have already approved the proposal. Therefore, the Japanese government expects that the meeting on the 27th will be passed. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will, in the name of Foreign Minister Uchida, send a telegram to League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond, without going through the Japanese delegation or embassies abroad, and simultaneously announce it in the official gazette and a statement in Tokyo. The scope of withdrawal is limited to the League of Nations Assembly and the Council, and other agencies will remain neither close nor separate, leaving room for rejoining the League of Nations at a later date. (United Press dispatch, 25th)

(Tokyo) Senior statesmen, elders, and both Presidents Suzuki and Wakatsuki initially disapproved of the military's proposal to withdraw from the League of Nations, arguing for self-restraint. However, the military coerced them with force, so they reluctantly complied. It is heard that the Privy Council also expressed dissatisfaction with Uchida's diplomacy, believing that Uchida is only a puppet of the military and has no diplomatic skills. If Uchida and Araki continue to wield their military swords for diplomacy, not only will Europe and the United States become enemies, but even in the Far East, they will not be able to gain friendly allies. The so-called Asian League is nothing more than a fool's dream. Therefore, at the plenary meeting on the 27th, the following hopes will be attached to request the passage of the original proposal: (1) Active direct negotiations between China and Japan must be carried out to quickly ease the deadlock of confrontation; (2) Military diplomacy must be carried out selectively. The current situation requires the domestic economic panic to be resolved, and the only way to do this is to stop China's boycott of Japanese goods. The opinions put forward by the Privy Council clearly imply a demand for Uchida's resignation, because as long as Araki and Uchida are in the court, Sino-Japanese negotiations cannot proceed. (United Press dispatch, 25th)

South Seas Mandate Island Issue

Japanese Navy's Strong Argument

(Tokyo) According to a Berlin dispatch, if the Japanese government withdraws from the League of Nations, the German government believes that the South Seas islands should be returned to the League of Nations, and substantively governed by the League of Nations, while formally hoping to return to Germany. It is rumored that preparations for negotiations have begun. The Japanese naval authorities have observed this as follows: According to Article 119 of the Treaty of Peace between the Allied and Associated Powers and Germany, the German government clearly ceded the German colonies to the Allied and Associated Powers. Therefore, Germany's return to this, although acknowledging its negotiations with the League of Nations and the Allied Powers, but negotiations with Japan, one of the Allied Powers, are not permissible, and are not allowed by Japan. If Germany has this intention, it is feared that this is caused by internal relations, and even if the South Seas islands are returned to Germany, it is feared that Britain and France will fear Germany's expansion of military power and will oppose it. Even the United States may not agree. The policy of the imperial government will not be moved, and it will have the following reasons why Japan can still possess the South Seas islands even though it has announced its withdrawal from the League of Nations: (1) Long-term entrusted governance, which is in fact owned by the trustee country, has been formally and informally clarified in several League of Nations Assemblies and Entrusted Governance Committees; (2) The German government abandoned the sovereignty of the entrusted governance area in the Treaty of Versailles, so it has no right to speak on this; (3) Non-member states can be trustee countries, such as the United States being the trustee country for Armenia, which is a precedent. (Dentsu dispatch, 25th)

Matsuoka Arrives in New York

Few Welcoming, Many Hating

Overseas Chinese Mr. Lin Detained for Carrying a Handgun

(New York) Japanese representative to the League of Nations Matsuoka Yosuke arrived in New York today aboard the Leviathan. Matsuoka met with reporters on deck, with a rather warm attitude, but his answers to reporters' questions revealed a challenging tone. Only a dozen or so local Japanese residents went to the pier to welcome him, while more than fifty people holding flags to protest Japan's invasion of Manchuria held demonstrations. Matsuoka immediately declared to the reporters that Japan was not a vassal state of the United States and had no obligation to explain its activities. He then explained that Japan had suffered greatly due to misunderstandings from all sides and the lack of proper publicity, saying that the United States was 5,000 miles away and it was difficult to fully understand Japan's various actions in Asia, just as Japan also found it difficult to understand the United States' occupation of several countries in the Western Hemisphere. He then explained that Japan wanted to take necessary actions to avoid the rise of dangerous conspiracies against Japan in Manchuria. He then discussed the League of Nations resolution, saying that whether to withdraw or not must be decided by the Japanese government. Finally, he said that he had no special mission in the United States, but only wanted to meet old friends and explain Japan's policies and position in Manchuria. As for the demonstrators, it was heard that only one Chinese person named Lin was detained for carrying a handgun, while the remaining forty-nine people were searched at the pier and then released. (National Telegraph, 24th)

Page 10

US Gold Embargo Lifted

Washington dispatch from the 24th: Treasury Secretary Woodin told reporters today that the announcement regarding the gold embargo is currently being prepared and may be announced tomorrow. Woodin did not express the content of this announcement. When asked whether the gold embargo would be lifted through announcement procedures, Woodin replied that he thought so. There are many rumors in New York's financial circles, saying that the authorities have lifted the gold embargo and that it will be announced soon. However, New York's financial circles expressed doubts about the possibility of not allowing unlimited exports of cash. If the embargo is completely lifted, it is impossible to calculate how much gold will be exported, because in addition to the cash held by foreign central banks in the United States, the number of foreigners holding US bonds and other items is also very large. Moreover, if domestic people want to transport gold out of the country, it should not be difficult, as long as they contact foreign merchants and ask them to withdraw cash on their behalf. The Treasury Secretary's remarks to reporters have attracted significant attention on Wall Street. The financial circles are eagerly awaiting the announcement that may be issued tomorrow. According to some opinions, cash exports to repay actual commercial debts may be allowed to go through, but they must follow strict licensing procedures.

Reuters dispatch from Washington, 24th: Senators who advocate maintaining the silver market expect that President Roosevelt will be sympathetic to them, so they are now preparing to re-promote the restoration of silver prices. In the next few days, Senator King will ask the White House to include at least three representatives related to silver in the delegation of the United States to the World Economic Conference. Senator Wheeler told guests that he would soon begin a campaign in the Senate to pass the silver bill with a ratio of sixteen to one. He believes that a legislative bill can be passed during the current congressional session to stabilize silver prices. He believes that passing the silver legislative bill is most appropriate today.

German Dictatorship Implemented

Reuters dispatch from Berlin, 24th: President Hindenburg signed the Enabling Act today, which stipulates that the National Socialist government is granted dictatorial power for a period of four years. It was passed by the parliament yesterday and took effect today. Now the dictatorial power will first be applied to a certain state in western Germany, which may expel Jews from the country.

National dispatch from Berlin, 24th: The German government held a cabinet meeting today, which lasted for a long time. Economic Minister Hugenberg first represented all cabinet members in congratulating Prime Minister Hitler on his success in parliament. Then, Interior Minister Frick proposed a general outline of domestic policy plans, the purpose of which is to coordinate the work of the federal government and various state cities. According to some newspaper reports, the cabinet also considered the proposal to implement the death penalty for political prisoners.

The Causes of the American Financial Panic (New York Correspondence)

Stock Market Prices Plunge, People Heavily in Debt

Banks Unable to Circulate, All Industries Greatly Affected

The world's first rich and powerful country, the leader of capitalist countries, the United States of America, which absorbs 42% of the world's total cash, has now reached the point of suspending the gold standard, and 15 million unemployed workers are on the verge of starvation. Middle- and upper-class families have also lost the image of their former prosperous lives. Among the 30 million workers in the United States, only half are fortunate enough to have jobs. The wages and salaries of some have been reduced by 20%, and some have even been reduced by 70%. On average, the actual reduction is 56.5%. The golden age of stocks, that is, ordinary stock dividends, could maintain a very comfortable life, but now it has become a dream.

The total value of stock market prices in 1929 was 346 billion US dollars, but now it is only worth 33.3 billion US dollars. Such a sharp drop is almost like a dream (the percentage of price drops has reached 92%). The debts of individuals and exchanges are estimated at 123 trillion US dollars, including 44 trillion US dollars in corporate debt, 57 trillion in real estate secured debt, and 20 trillion US dollars in rural debt. These new debtors, in 1928 and 1929, one US dollar now has to pay 33 cents of interest. In 1929, the national income of the United States was 85 trillion, but last year the income was only 49 trillion US dollars, of which one-fifth was eaten up by interest.

If private debt is so huge, what about the national accounting? The total amount of US national debt is estimated at 208.6 billion US dollars, which has increased by 38.75 billion US dollars since 1929. In the past seven months of the 1933 fiscal year, revenue was insufficient, already 12.71721021 billion US dollars. At the end of January last year, the US national debt was only 178.15861117 billion US dollars, but at the end of January this year, it increased to 208.11707134 billion US dollars. In reality, the national debt increased by 30 trillion US dollars. If it were not for the assistance of the banking groups in New York, the world's major capital and the den of sin in Chicago, all national industries would go bankrupt. "Tammany" (Democratic Club), which holds the bull's ears of New York City politics, cannot but bow to the banking groups. It is not known that although the national income has shrunk, the value of the "gold dollar" has reversed and risen. Compared with 1929, the general cost of living has decreased by 22%. This means that one dollar three years ago is now worth one dollar and thirty-three cents. In other words, fewer "gold dollars" could be used to purchase more goods three years ago. People who borrowed money three years ago have to repay one gold dollar with one dollar and thirty-three cents. Therefore, those in the debtor class who used to pay six percent interest now have to pay eight percent interest. As for farmers, it is even worse, because the prices of agricultural products have plummeted. For example, if they borrowed 2,000 US dollars with a guarantee of harvesting wheat, the market price of wheat was one US dollar per bushel (about 3.6 liters in our country) four years ago, then 2,000 yuan would have to be repaid with 2,000 "bushels" of wheat. The current market value is less than 50 cents, and at least more than double must be paid to the creditor, that is, 4,000 bushels of wheat are enough to repay the debt. What a grim sight this is.

On the first day that President Roosevelt took office, he encountered a "financial panic." The world's "gold" king is about to fall from his throne. The first thing he wants to do is to restructure the value of the "gold dollar," and "if the value of the gold dollar does not increase, then it will be even more difficult for the American people to live." Senator Borah once said,

"In 1929, the total national income of the United States was 85 trillion US dollars, but last year (1932) it was only 37 trillion. If we calculate it by averaging all men, women, and children in the country, the average income per person in 1929 was 700 US dollars, but now it has been reduced to 300 US dollars. However, each person still has to bear the federal government, state government, city government, and other taxes, about 77 US dollars, and the burden of fixed interest is also assumed to be 77 US dollars. Then the national income in 1932 would only be 145 US dollars, which means that the average cost of living per person per month is only 12 US dollars..."

In this situation, in the country with the world's highest standard of living, the plight of the people of the United States of America, even if it is not a living hell, but the unemployed people living in small houses by the Hudson River, have no unemployment insurance and no work, only to starve with their eyes open. At the same time, the financial capitalists on Wall Street have money but nowhere to spend it. The countries of South America have announced the suspension of all debts, and a portion of US investment cannot be recovered. European countries should be better than South America, but there is probably no hope of repaying war debts. The golden dream of the Far East market has been shattered by Japan's iron fist. Now I really don't know what the future holds. The solution to the war debt problem, the abolition of tariff barriers, the reduction of armaments, the international economic conference, the opportunity to gain equality in Manchuria, the open-door policy, etc., are all major problems facing the United States, which must be resolved in order to find a way out. However, the general public seems very indifferent to these things, and in fact lacks understanding. What they want is to reduce the value of currency, open new avenues for domestic and foreign trade, restore past prosperity, raise prices, and increase the purchasing power of the general public.

However, credit is frozen, people's hearts are purified, and the issuance of temporary currencies in various states is prevalent. The turnover of banks is even more sluggish. The financial frenzy that swept from Michigan has spread all over the United States today. Banks have closed their doors everywhere. Yesterday was a millionaire, but overnight he became penniless. Although ordinary stores have not closed down, everyone has no money to buy things, and their business has to wait. The announcement of bank closures seems to have a very weak relationship with the middle- and lower-class families who have been poor to the extreme. The rich are trapped even more severely.

"Barter" is a form of society in primitive times. Unexpectedly, it is seen in the American society, which has reached the pinnacle of modern civilization, during the financial panic. According to our common sense, and after studying the general economic situation, this situation will certainly not continue for a long time, but the people of the United States will suffer even more, and I don't know when they will recover their prosperity. (New York, March 5, 1933)

Japanese Troops

Communist Movement Actively Spreading

The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun reported on the 15th that the Kinrin Yoshida branch of the Kyoto City Sakyo Ward Reservists Association had been collecting comfort bags for troops stationed in Manchuria from the general public in the ward since the 20th of last month until the 3rd of this month, and had collected more than 2,000 bags. Unexpectedly, in each bag, a large number of anti-military documents aimed at communizing the military were suddenly discovered. The association immediately reported to the military police. As a result of the investigation, the sender was identified as Nakayama Noboru, the owner of a signboard business at No. 9 Yoshida Shimoadachi Town, Sakyo Ward, Kyoto City. A few years ago, he was a leftist. This time, he took the opportunity to attempt to communize the army, falsely donating to soldiers stationed in Manchuria in the name of condolences, and secretly sealed red cloths one shaku five sun long and two shaku wide, wrapped in cultural struggles, literary news, and various reactionary news, into the comfort bags, in order to distribute them to the soldiers at the front.

The Tokyo Nichi-Nichi Shimbun also reported on the 15th that after a general inspection of the executives of the Writers' League, it was learned that a Pan-Pacific Anti-Imperialist Shanghai Conference was scheduled to be convened at the end of March, and demonstrations were to be held on commemorative days such as March 5th and 15th. What is most alarming is that they planned to mobilize all factories extensively and cooperate with the Anti-Imperialist League's Jōhoku Ward to connect junior high schools, military supplies factories, and grocery stores in the virgin lands of communism. Fortunately, the Ikebukuro police station discovered it in advance and arrested 17 leaders, who confessed that there were 300 to 400 accomplices, who used film, drama, and music to unite comrades and promote leftist ideas such as "Red Flag," "Anti-New," and "Anti-Imperialism News."

Harbin and Hailar Under the Puppet Flag

The Current Situation in Harbin Forms a Hell

The People of Hailar Have All Fled

Harbin

Harbin Communication: Since the Japanese invasion and occupation of Harbin on February 6th of last year, the people have been living in a sea of misery. The market is depressed, all industries are withering, education has been severely damaged, and a large percentage of children have dropped out of school. Bandits are everywhere, and gambling and opium are rampant. The once prosperous commercial port has been transformed into a hell. The details are as follows: (1) Japanese soldiers kill wantonly and inhumanely. Since the Japanese army invaded Harbin, any Chinese, whether farmers, workers, or businessmen, who accidentally offended Japanese residents were lightly beaten and arrested, and heavily shot and killed. Usually, when Japanese soldiers went out, they abused the people in every possible way. Even on trams, Japanese soldiers often interrogated fellow laborers sitting next to them, asking, "What country are you from?" If they answered, "Chinese," the Japanese soldiers would whip them. They would ask again, "What country are you from?" The laborers, thinking they were already subjugated, dared to call themselves Japanese, and would answer "Japanese." The Japanese soldiers would then beat them even harder and ask again. If they answered, "Korean," the Japanese soldiers would become furious, raise their guns, and pretend to shoot. Someone sitting nearby secretly told them to say "Manchukuo people," and they were spared from death. Such incidents of innocent people being killed are countless, and it is truly tragic. (2) Businesses close, people struggle to survive. After the Japanese puppets seized the Northeast Customs, they imposed heavy taxes on Chinese goods. Therefore, the goods on the market are all Japanese goods. However, the market has been devastated by the Japanese, and suffered from flood damage. In addition, the reckless issuance of banknotes has caused financial chaos, and the people are generally poor. With their purchasing power lost, businesses have been forced to close. Even those few who manage to barely survive are deserted and make no profit. Major firms, such as Gong He Li, Da Luo Xin, and Tong Fa Long, are considering closing down due to excessive losses. The Japanese puppets, fearing that their closure would cause panic in the market, have prevented them from doing so, leaving these stores in a difficult position, forced to accept losses. (3) Schools close, the number of vagrants increases. After the former Zhang Huanxiang expanded the special zone schools, the number of middle schools increased to more than ten, and there were about 300 elementary schools and more than 40 civilian schools. Recently, the Japanese have been actively destroying them, causing all middle schools to close and the school buildings to be used as barracks. Only six elementary schools remain open, using textbooks that aim to dumb down the population, with Japanese as the main subject. Civilian schools no longer exist. Harbin originally had a Sino-Russian joint venture industrial university with about a thousand Chinese students. The curriculum was rigorous, and graduates all served in society. Although it has not been affected by the war due to its relationship with Russia, the Chinese students have been deeply stimulated by being with Russian students, and they have all successively dropped out and joined the army. Other examples include the commercial university building being used as a Japanese military garrison, the second building of the law and political university being used as a puppet police station, and the Harbin Library being used as a puppet guard post, which are particularly disheartening. In total, more than 30,000 students in Harbin have dropped out of school. (4) Opium and gambling are open, prostitutes are like ants. The Japanese plan to use policies to weaken and fool the people, so opium and gambling are open and licenses are issued to collect taxes. People with weak knowledge, unaware of the enemy's scheme, rush to it. In Daowai, Harbin alone, there are more than 6,000 opium dens. The large number of addicts is self-evident. Furthermore, there are Japanese who sell morphine and heroin everywhere. Gambling games such as Pai Gow, lottery, Sic Bo, and Mahjong are all available. Gambling dens are called clubs. The number of people who have been bankrupted is unknown. As a result, prostitutes are like ants and bandits are rampant. Street kidnappings and indoor scams are common. (5) Soldiers are treated like prisoners, police are treated like enemies. Except for high-ranking officers, the puppet troops all want to revolt. The Japanese know this well and are very strict in their prevention. In addition to sending Japanese trainers and officers to the teams, they dare not issue ammunition in large quantities. Each soldier is only issued 200 bullets during combat, and only a few dozen at other times. At night, firearms are locked in the armory to prevent mutiny. Soldiers in the Miller camp even have to hand in their shoes and socks at night, which are locked in a room. They have to walk barefoot to go to the toilet. They are treated like prisoners. The police are even more mistreated. In the recent reorganization of the police department, Japanese occupy four out of the seven major section chief positions. (6) The people are eager to recover lost territory. Since our country blocked postal and telegraphic communications, the Northeast has been cut off from the interior. Harbin newspapers are used by the Japanese to spread propaganda that is unfavorable to our country. Except for those who are willing to act as accomplices for the

Page 11

Japanese, the general public is eager for our government to recover lost territory as soon as possible. If our government is determined to confront Japan and unite, then the people of the Northeast will certainly rise up and respond.

Hailar

The Miller Review reported a communication from a foreigner in Harbin saying, "I traveled from Hailar to Harbin. The train was extremely crowded and there were not enough vehicles to meet the demand because when the Soviet Union saw the arrival of the Japanese army, they moved the best locomotives and trains across the border. The police first entered the train to check travel permits, and then a Japanese officer who came with them asked each passenger for a business card. For those he suspected, he personally checked them one by one. This Japanese officer glanced at the Chinese passengers sitting in the same carriage as me, raised his thumb, and made a sound to signal them to stand up. The Chinese passengers all changed color, angry but afraid to speak. If these Chinese had ever had any good feelings towards 'Manchukuo,' judging by what they told me after this Japanese officer left, they clearly expressed that they had already sided with the other side. No forts were seen along the way, but the buildings occupied by the Japanese were almost all surrounded by railway networks. Drunken Japanese soldiers constantly roamed Hailar, acting as if they were conquerors. While I was waiting for the train, a Harbin train arrived carrying twenty Japanese prostitutes. Someone told me that whenever the Japanese army entered a city or town, a batch of prostitutes would follow. Hailar is already like a dead cave. After four o'clock in the afternoon, there are no pedestrians on the street. Prices have fallen for everything, especially meat, butter, fish, and firewood, but there are no buyers. The Chinese residents have all fled, united in their hatred of the Japanese. The term 'Manchukuo' is regarded as a curse. On the train, I wanted a rag to wipe the seat, and a soldier calling himself 'Manchukuo' gave me a 'Manchukuo' flag instead, as if to know what he was thinking. The Japanese army occupied Hailar without firing a shot. On December 3rd and 4th, General Su Bingwen's troops left Hailar on three trains, and the next day three trains of Japanese troops entered the city. The Mongols in the Hailar area generally sympathize with the Japanese because they are dissatisfied with the treatment of the Chinese. The Japanese are spreading rumors that the Chinese will colonize all of Mongolia, convert it into farming areas, and end the nomadic life of the Mongols."

Japanese Army

Failed to Attack Dongjiakou

Appropriately transporting the remains of fallen officers and soldiers back to Shenyang

And building defensive works to quietly await reinforcements

Beiping Communication: On the Xifengkou front, on the morning of the 21st, the enemy army launched a fierce attack, and fierce battles broke out along the entire line. Our army calmly responded. That evening, the enemy stopped attacking and retreated to the Baitaizi position. Today (22nd), there were only local conflicts on the front lines. For example, in the Dongjiakou area, a combined force of enemy infantry, artillery, and cavalry, numbering about a thousand, attacked at 8:00 AM this morning, but also failed. More than 20 Japanese aircraft also flew to Zunhua Santunying for bombing. Outside Luowenyu, the Japanese army has retreated to the Banbishan and Foyeshan areas, constructing defensive works nearby. The enemy's reinforcements have moved towards Huangyaguan. A certain division of our army stationed in Malanguan is closely guarding against them. Song Zheyuan, the commander-in-chief of the Twenty-ninth Army, accompanied by Kong Xiangxi, Pang Bingxun, Xiao Zhenying, Yu Feipeng, etc., arrived at a certain place near Zunhua at 10:00 PM tonight and will go to the Luowenyu front tomorrow morning for inspection. A certain important person who came from the front line to Peiping this morning said that the results of the fierce fighting near Shanchayu outside Luowenyu in the previous days showed that the enemy suffered heavy casualties and corpses were scattered everywhere. Division Commander Liu Ruming has already taken photos of the uniforms and insignia of two enemy colonels found on the battlefield and will send them to Peiping within days. Near Diaoyutai, the enemy has had wounded soldiers for more than eight days. The remains of the fallen officers and soldiers were mostly burned by the Japanese army. The remains of an important military officer have been sent back to Pingquan and transported back to Shenyang by plane.

Liu Shifu, the director of the Beiping office of Song Zheyuan's troops, said today that Zhou, a member of our army's staff, returned to Peiping from the front this morning. According to him, in the Luowenyu area, the enemy troops have been repelled by our Liu Ruming's division to about 20 miles outside the pass. The enemy troops are grabbing civilians there to build fortifications and prepare for defense. Judging by their intentions, they seem to be quietly awaiting reinforcements. Starting today, our soldiers on the front lines are clearing the battlefield. According to local residents, the enemy army suffered heavy casualties after being attacked by us. In addition to transporting some of the wounded by car, on the 20th, the enemy sent several planes to the area to transport away five or six bodies of officers above the rank of captain. There are still five or six hundred bodies on the battlefield. In this battle, from the 9th to the 11th, the enemy army attacked us with planes, tanks, heavy artillery, and a large number of troops. Our army took a defensive posture, seemingly completely passive. Since the 12th, after our army destroyed the enemy's artillery positions, the enemy was unable to resist. Our army then launched surprise attacks on the fields every night. The enemy was unable to defend against our army, and thus our army changed from being passive to being active. (22nd)

Chen Jitang Returns to Guangzhou

Tan Sui talks about Chen's assassination attempt

The assassin was captured and executed on the spot

Guangzhou Communication: After Chen Jitang encountered danger in Jieyang during his inspection of the East River, he turned to Chaozhou and Meizhou, passing through Xingning, Laolong, and Heyuan. On the 16th night, he arrived in Huizhou. He left Huizhou at 12:00 PM and went to Zhangmutou Station on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, taking a pre-arranged special train to Guangzhou overnight. He arrived in Guangzhou at 5:50 AM on the 17th and went back to the model village residence in Dongshan for rest. Military and political circles went to express their condolences. Chen briefly spoke for a moment, and the visitors were dismissed. Chen, feeling tired from the journey, was unable to speak at length, so he sent Tan Sui, the chief of staff of the Second Army, who accompanied him on the inspection, to receive the guests. According to Tan, Chen first took the Haizhou warship to Shanwei during his inspection of the East River. He landed in Shanwei and passed through Haifeng, Lufeng, Kuitan, and Puning. On the morning of the 7th, he arrived in Jieyang from Puning, where he encountered danger. When Chen landed in Jieyang, a person resembling a messenger handed him a document in the welcoming crowd at the pier. Chen received and opened the document. Suddenly, the messenger revealed malicious intent. His left hand tightly held Chen's belt, and his right hand reached into his pocket to grab a hand grenade, intending to throw it at Chen. Chen noticed this and immediately hugged the assailant tightly to prevent the grenade from being thrown. The entourage saw this dangerous situation, and Zhang Ruigui, the commander of the Independent Second Division, stepped forward and knocked the assailant's left hand away. The entourage protected Chen from danger, pushing the assailant away. The assailant stumbled to the ground, and the hand grenade exploded at the same time, wounding 15 guards and killing two. The assailant was also injured and arrested on the spot. According to his confession, he was a communist. He was then taken out and executed by the defense army. After Chen escaped danger, he left Jieyang that day and went to Shantou, staying for three days. On the morning of the 9th, he passed through Chaoan to Meixian. After inspecting Jiaoling from Meixian, he then added Meixian city. From Meixian, he passed through Xingning and Wuhua, arriving at Laolong on the 14th and Heyuan on the 15th. On the night of the 16th, he arrived in Huizhou late at night. He left Huizhou from Zhangmutou Station, taking a special train to Guangzhou. During this trip through the eastern districts, he inspected the Fifth Division, the Third Army, the Second Independent Division, and the First Independent Division, and gave speeches to the troops. Chen gave speeches everywhere he went, generally explaining the Guangdong provincial government's determination to implement a three-year administration plan, abolish all exorbitant taxes, relieve the people's suffering, and hoped that the people would realize local autonomy and unite against foreign enemies.

Liu Ruiheng Talks About

Frontline Rescue Situation

There is a Considerable Organization

Rescue is Not a Problem

Jinan Communication: Liu Ruiheng, the director of the Central Health Administration and chairman of the North China Rescue Association, returned to Beijing from Peiping. This morning, the reporter interviewed Mr. Liu on the train and asked about the war situation and rescue efforts on the front lines. According to him, in recent days, there have been no fierce battles in Xifengkou and Gubeikou except for Luowenyu. The Rescue Association has taken in and rescued more than 2,000 wounded soldiers from Song Zheyuan's troops, more than 3,000 from the Central government's directly subordinate divisions, and more than 1,000 each from Wang Yizhe's and Sun Dianying's troops, totaling 7,000 to 8,000. More than 3,000 are in Beiping, more than 2,000 are in Tongzhou, more than 1,000 are in Kangzhuang, and the rest are in various places. The Japanese propaganda that we have many wounded soldiers is unreliable. Two-thirds of the wounded are lightly wounded, mostly from aircraft bombs. When the North China Rescue Association was first established, it was quite difficult due to the hasty organization and insufficient personnel. The hospitals of various armies were also not fully equipped. Now there are 12 rescue teams, each with a dozen or so doctors and nurses, plus several dozen stretcher bearers, distributed in Beiping, Miyun, Zunhua, Jizhou, Tongzhou, Kangzhuang, Sanhe, and other places for rescue. Wounded soldiers from Gubeikou are first transported to Miyun, and wounded soldiers from Xifengkou are first transported to Zunhua, and then transported to Tongzhou and Beiping. Wounded soldiers from Sun Dianying's troops are transported from Zhangjiakou to Kangzhuang. The Central Rear Military Hospital has also been established in Baoding, Shunde, and other places, on a very large scale. Various charitable organizations in Peiping and Tianjin have also organized themselves voluntarily, so there are enough hospital doctors, and they are working very hard. The funding is all self-raised or donated by various parties, so as long as the front-line troops can fight, rescue is not a problem. I have returned to Beijing to handle everything because the northern rescue matters are already being enthusiastically handled by Xiong Bing and other committee members, and the affairs of the Central Hospital and the Health Administration are also very busy. The overall national health renovation plan has not been actively implemented due to the situation and funding issues. (24th)

Qingdao Organizes Local Association

Donate One Year of Land Rent and Land Tax

Civil Servants Donate Half a Month's Salary

Qingdao Communication: Since the loss of Rehe, North China has been shocked. The cities of Peiping and Tianjin have organized local associations, raising donations in various ways to share the national crisis. All sectors in Qingdao have risen up in response and are now organizing a local association to conduct large-scale national salvation fundraising in order to defend themselves and defend the country. It is planned to first donate one year of land rent and land tax. Other fundraising methods are being discussed. Shen Honglie, the commander of the navy and mayor of Qingdao, also believes that civil servants are members of the nation and should not be left behind in defending the country. It is the time to destroy the family to relieve the country. The city government and the navy headquarters have jointly determined the donation methods as follows: (1) This donation is named the National Salvation Special Donation. (2) All staff members of the city government and the navy headquarters will donate half a month's salary once, according to their current actual salary, in three monthly installments, starting from this month. (3) Naval soldiers and city police, as well as workers in the city government and navy headquarters, will donate according to four grades: 3 yuan for Yuan grade, 2 yuan for Xiang grade, 1 yuan for Li grade, and 5 jiao for Zhen grade, with personal freedom to donate, limited to one time. (4) After the implementation of the above measures, all previous monthly donations of 1% for disaster relief will be stopped immediately. The allocated donations should be deducted after this donation is deducted. In addition to the navy, which is ordered by the navy headquarters, the city government has instructed all subordinate bureaus and stations to comply. (24th)

Songjiang

Provincial Order to Arrest Bandit Collaborators

The county government received a secret telegram from the Director of Civil Affairs of Jiangsu Province, approving the inquiry from the Civil Affairs Department of Zhejiang Province regarding Zhou Qingfan, also known as Zhou Qinghuai, suspected of selling guns to kidnapper Fan Bingfa. County Magistrate Shen immediately sent a secret telegram to Zhang Jilin, the director of the Fengjing Second Branch Bureau, to arrest and interrogate him. Zhou Qingfan used to be the chief of the Fengjing Security Corps. Since Fan Bingfa's kidnapping case was discovered, Jiashan County of Zhejiang Province has summoned him many times without success, and the Civil Affairs Department has reported him for arrest. Director Zhang of the branch bureau will find a way to summon Zhou Qingfan, escort him to the county government today (25th), and detain him temporarily, waiting to be reported to the Civil Affairs Department for handling.

Joint Patrol of Water and Land Police on a Regular Basis

The Nine-County Joint Defense Office recently ordered the water and land police teams of various counties to hold joint patrols. This county ordered the water patrol team and police team to set off on a regular basis and hold joint patrols in Jinshanwei. Fan Zhicheng, the captain of the first team of the first district of the provincial public security team, also held joint patrols with the Qingpu water police team in Fanbang New Town and other places to arrest bandits and maintain local peace.

Wuxi

Rice Business Tax Issue Resolved

The Wuxi rice industry, in the urban and rural areas, is divided into eight sections, with more than 130 lines. Due to the decline of the rice market and sluggish business, the lines have been closing down one after another. The nature of the business is mostly reselling among the same industry, which is completely different from the situation in other counties. Even the same industry in the eight sections is different. Therefore, they still failed to declare the business tax for the previous year in accordance with the regulations. The bureau, however, is limited by the regulations, and the provincial order urges the declaration urgently. It has repeatedly sent personnel to investigate, resulting in a conflict between the investigator and Pan Lugang, the owner of Jianyi Rice Bank outside the South Gate, constituting two crimes of obstructing official duties and injury. The lawsuit is still unresolved. Recently, the county chamber of commerce discussed with the county government to negotiate with both parties repeatedly, and the intentions gradually approached. Yesterday (25th) morning, the chamber of commerce invited more than 30 section directors from the eight rice industry sections to discuss the matter at the meeting. County Magistrate Chen and Xia, the director of the Business Tax Bureau, attended the meeting. As a result, it was decided that the industry association would report first with the lines. The total amount of all taxes, starting from the autumn of the 21st year, will be 10,000 yuan for the whole year. Regarding the re-examination of the accounts, the industry association will send personnel to assist the Business Tax Bureau in the joint investigation. At this point, the rice industry business tax, which has been deadlocked for half a year, can be resolved.

Fifth District Township Head Robbed Three Times

Lu Huiyun, the township head of Liujiadang Township in the Fifth District of the county, has a well-to-do family and has long been coveted by bandits. On the night of the first of this month, six or seven bandits robbed him with weapons, causing hundreds of yuan in losses. The victim, Lu Huiyun, was also tied up and beaten by the bandits. The case has been reported to the 13th branch bureau of public security and the security corps for investigation and arrest. Unexpectedly, ten days later, on the night of the 14th, more bandits came to Lu's house to rob. The door had been broken. Lu's whole family was asleep. Fortunately, the villagers heard the alarm and rang the gongs to call for help. The bandits fled in panic. Afterwards, the Fifth District Security Corps believed that Lu's house had been robbed twice, which was detrimental to local security, so it sent 10 corps members armed with weapons to patrol the Sitou area of Liujiadang all night. However, on the night of the day before yesterday (24th) at 9:00 PM, more than a dozen armed bandits came to Lu's house for the third time to rob. Lu's family members climbed onto the roof and shouted wildly. The villagers rushed to the scene, and the bandits were frightened away. The security corps and police officers also rushed to the scene after hearing the news, and arrested one bandit on the spot. He has been escorted to the bureau and transferred to the city for interrogation and detention. The remaining bandits are being pursued.

Fengxian

Lian Huaipu Died in Battle Against Japan

Lian Huaipu, a native of the county, joined the army in the 16th year of the Republic of China and was under the command of Xu Tingyao, the former commander of the Fourth Division. He accumulated military merits and was transferred to the 25th Division under Guan Linzheng, serving as the commander of the 3rd machine gun company. This time, he was ordered to set off to the front line to fight against the enemy, and he died heroically in the battle of Gubeikou. The 3rd Machine Gun Company of the 149th Regiment of the division has informed his family by letter and has buried the martyr's remains in Miyun County, Hebei Province. All sectors in the county were shocked and mourned after hearing the bad news. In addition to launching a memorial service by the county, district, party, and government agencies on the same day, they also sent a telegram to the front to inquire about the circumstances of the Lian martyr's death on that day in order to commend him.

Changshu

Water Police Extort Cattle Dealers

A certain Xie, the captain of the water police detachment stationed in Fushan, seized 22 heads of plowing cattle in Dengshi the other day. Xie confiscated them because private sales of plowing cattle violated the ban. It turned out that the cattle were actually yellow cattle, not plowing cattle. Therefore, the two town chiefs, Lang and Zhang, were asked to intercede. After paying 100 yuan, they were released. On the afternoon of the 23rd, 18 yellow cattle were transported through Lihua. The water police stationed there immediately stopped them and did not allow them to pass, and brought the cattle to the guardhouse. The cattle dealers then bribed them with 60 yuan, but they refused. That night, two policemen were guarding the cattle. Unexpectedly, the cattle dealers secretly took them away one by one. When the police learned the news, they went to chase them. Suddenly, dozens of people rushed out in the coastal area and surrounded and beat the police officer Zhou Xuekun, who was seriously injured and stabbed in the leg. Then they dispersed.

Jiangyin

Firecracker Shop Explosion Injures People

Xu Guangheng Firecracker Shop, located in the east of Beiwaitan Alley, is quite prosperous and has business in various counties of Jiangsu and Changzhou. There are more than 20 shop assistants. These days, they are rushing to ship goods and also work at night. At midnight on the 24th, shop assistant Tang Hongwu was making firecrackers. Due to hammering nails on gunpowder, a loud explosion occurred, shaking down the second row of houses and injuring Zhang Xisheng, Xia Yueqing, Liu Manlang, Liu Shulan, Xue Shengyu, Bian Asi, and shop owner Xu Hongtang, seven people in total. Most of their clothes were burned and their faces and arms were burned. All were sent to Lunyuan Hospital for treatment. Among them, three people were seriously injured, but their lives were not in danger.

Danyang

Seizure of Smuggled Opium

Yue Tianbao, a resident of Raozhuang Bridge in the South Township, came from Shanghai on a regular ship yesterday, carrying a large amount of smuggled opium. A plainclothes detective from the county government found out and seized two large wooden boxes full of 54 bags of opium, weighing more than 740 taels, on the ship. The witnesses were also escorted to the county. Shen Cheng, the judge, opened the court for interrogation. His confession was ambiguous. He was ordered to be sent to prison to await trial.

Zhenjiang

Wang Jiwu Embezzlement of Office

Wang Jiwu, the current magistrate of Danyang County, was interrogated by the Zhenjiang Court for embezzling seized opium and forging reward receipts while serving as the magistrate of Jingjiang County. The debate ended the day before yesterday, and the sentence was scheduled to be pronounced yesterday. It is said that Wang has decided to appeal.

Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Storm Resolved

The Zhenjiang Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Bureau could not make ends meet due to excessive quotas and negotiated with merchants to increase them. The Tobacco Merchants Association expressed its opposition. Because of the weak market and dull life, it was difficult to increase. Both sides expressed their difficulties. Hu Xiwu, the chairman of the industry association, proposed a method to consider both sides and asked the chamber of commerce to assist in mediation. After two months of negotiations, it has been properly resolved. All unanimously paid taxes and obtained licenses in accordance with procedures.

Nantong

Langshan Will Collapse into the Yangtze River

The Nantong riverbank has collapsed severely recently. Langshan was originally more than 20 miles away from the riverbank, but now it is approaching, and it will enter the river sooner or later. Local groups have convened an emergency meeting to protect against collapse and decided to request the province to send a commissioner to investigate immediately and allocate road building mu donations as funds for protecting against collapse in order to rescue and relieve the disaster.

Hangzhou

Business Community Raises Funds for Airplane Donation

The Zhejiang Provincial Airplane Fundraising Committee has stipulated that the business, industry, government, academic, and other circles in the province should each donate funds for one airplane. It is understood that purchasing one airplane for the business community requires funds ranging from 120,000 to 150,000 yuan. It has been decided that the fundraising amounts for the chambers of commerce in various locations will be divided into five classes: A, B, C, D, and E. Class A is 8,000 yuan, Class B is 4,000 yuan, Class C is 2,000 yuan, Class D is 1,000 yuan, and Class E is 500 yuan. The assigned fundraising quotas are as follows: 23,500 yuan for counties and cities under the jurisdiction of Hangzhou, 18,500 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Jiaxing, 18,500 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Huzhou, 17,000 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Ningbo, 21,500 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Shaoxing, 10,000 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Taizhou, 11,000 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Jinhua, 6,000 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Quzhou, 5,500 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Yan'an, 12,000 yuan for counties under the jurisdiction of Wenzhou, and 6,500 yuan for the Chuzhou region.

Ningbo

Robbery Case in Dongsheng Village

Sheng Shanren, a resident of Dongsheng Village in Luotuo Bridge, Cixi East, is employed at an arts and crafts company in Shanghai. His wife and three maids were left at home. Unexpectedly, at around 4 a.m. yesterday (the 23rd), seven robbers suddenly arrived, armed with weapons, and broke into the house. Local News

Wang Jingwei and Sun Ke Returned to Nanjing Together Last Night

Mr. Wang said he was going to meet with Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission.

The Premier of the Executive Yuan May Be Announced Tomorrow

Mr. Wang Jingwei has repeatedly expressed his humility regarding the position of Premier of the Executive Yuan. After a resolution by the Central Standing Committee, Mr. Sun Ke and Mr. Gu Mengyu were dispatched to Shanghai, one after the other, to persuade him to stay. Mr. Sun Ke arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning and immediately went to meet with Mr. Wang. The outcome of their conversation was quite satisfactory, and Mr. Wang's intention to resign may have been dispelled. At 11:30 p.m. last night, Mr. Sun Ke and Mr. Wang returned to Nanjing together. The details are recorded as follows:

Sun Ke Arrived in Shanghai

The two representatives dispatched by the Central Government to persuade Mr. Wang Jingwei to stay, Mr. Sun Ke and Mr. Gu Mengyu, apart from Mr. Gu, who had already arrived in Shanghai the night before to visit Mr. Wang and persuade him to stay, Mr. Sun also left Beijing by night train the night before, arriving in Shanghai at around 8 a.m. yesterday. After getting off the train, Mr. Sun first returned to his Shanghai residence at 22 Columbia Road for a brief rest.

Sun Ke and Wu Tiecheng Visited Mr. Wang

At 9 a.m., he went to Mr. Wang's residence on Route Ghisi to meet and talk with Mr. Wang, and conveyed the intentions of the Central Government, requesting that Mr. Wang immediately go to Nanjing to resume his duties. Mr. Wang initially declined humbly, but after Mr. Sun's sincere persuasion, and because Ms. Soong was unwilling to continue in the role, Mr. Wang finally agreed to go to Nanjing that day to discuss the selection of a successor. After talking in detail for an hour, Mr. Sun left at 10:10 a.m. At 10:20 a.m., Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng continued to visit, inquiring about Mr. Wang's opinions on resuming his duties and offering his persuasion, before leaving at 10:40 a.m.

Mr. Wang's Remarks

After Mr. Sun's visit, Mr. Wang personally saw him off and then made remarks to the reporters of the New Sound News Agency, saying that he had resigned from his position at the Central Government and proposed that Ms. Soong succeed him. After arriving in Shanghai, he immediately visited Ms. Soong, asking her to formally take over the position. However, because Ms. Soong's responsibilities in handling finances were also extremely heavy, she could not concurrently hold the position of Premier of the Executive Yuan. Therefore, the Central Government ordered him to take on the role. This morning, after the results of his meeting with Mr. Sun, it was decided that the issue of the Premier of the Executive Yuan would be discussed after arriving in Nanjing, and another suitable successor would be decided upon. If there is still no suitable candidate, then whether or not he will resume his duties will be further discussed. As for the time and place of his meeting with Chairman Jiang, because it concerns military matters, it is difficult to announce for the time being. His tone suggested that his intention to resign had been dispelled. In addition, Mr. Wang also stated that rumors that he resigned due to differences of opinion were completely untrue, and that the work of the Executive Yuan had not been suspended due to his resignation.

Mr. Sun's Remarks

The President of the Legislative Yuan, Sun Ke, received reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Columbia Road at 11 p.m. last night and made remarks, saying that Chairman Jiang plans to make a trip south within one or two days. Mr. Wang, after our delegation conveyed the Central Government's wishes and earnestly persuaded him to stay, agreed to go to Nanjing this evening (i.e., last night). The issue of resuming his position as Premier of the Executive Yuan will be discussed again after arriving in Nanjing. According to my conjecture, it is hoped that his intention to resign will be dispelled. Because the duties of the Premier of the Executive Yuan are heavy, apart from Mr. Wang and Ms. Soong, there is really no suitable candidate for the time being. It is also the intention of the various committees of the Central Government that Mr. Wang is the only one who can do it. Mr. Wang decided to go to Nanjing tonight (i.e., last night), and I plan to travel with him.

Returned to Nanjing Last Night

At 11:30 p.m. last night, the President of the Legislative Yuan, Sun Ke, accompanied by Wang Jingwei and his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, the Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, Tang Youren, and others, took two special carriages attached to the Beijing-Shanghai night train to Nanjing. The security at the station was extremely tight. According to what Mr. Wang told reporters on the train, Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission may come south from the front line today (i.e., yesterday) for a meeting. As for the Premier of the Executive Yuan, it is hoped that Ms. Soong will take on the difficult task. When reporters asked if Ms. Soong firmly declined, whether Mr. Wang would agree to resume his duties, Mr. Wang said, "We'll talk about it when we get to Nanjing. It should be decided tomorrow (the 26th), and the successor to the new Premier will definitely be announced the day after tomorrow (the 27th." Furthermore, according to Mr. Sun, the Central Government hopes that Mr. Wang will return to his position, and it is likely to be realized.

The preparations for the accommodation of all parties are recorded below:

Number of People Arriving

When they departed from Vladivostok, there were originally 188 people, including 19 wounded soldiers and 11 family members of Brigade Commander Zheng, who had already landed in Tianjin and gone to Beiping for residence and medical treatment. The actual number of people arriving in Shanghai is 158. In addition to Commander Wang's wife and children, Brigade Commanders Liu and Kong also came with them. When Liu and others arrive in Shanghai, due to their unfamiliarity with the place, in order to avoid unscrupulous people taking advantage of the situation, the army headquarters specially issued certificate documents for proof to avoid trouble.

Accommodation Location

The family members of Commander Wang and others were initially planned to be accommodated at the Shanghai Injured Soldiers' Hospital in West Shanghai. Among them, it had been decided that Commander Wang's wife and children would live in Room 31 on the third floor, Brigade Commander Kong would live in Room 31, and Brigade Commander Liu and his wife would live in Room 23 on the second floor. The rest had not yet been decided. The cost of food and accommodation is 77 cents per person per day, half price for children under the age of 14. The total daily expenses are estimated to be around 100 yuan.
