Second Collection Results for Saving the Nation Through Aviation

Total Reached Over 290,000 Yuan

The Fresh Meat Industry Plans to Raise 100,000 Yuan Independently

At 4 p.m. yesterday, the Shanghai City Collection Team of the Chinese Aviation Association held its second results report at the YMCA. The total team leader Wu Tiecheng and the various team leaders Cai Zengji, Lai Zhenhuan, Yang Nianzu, Li Tingan, Wang Yinting, Qian Jinhua, Tong Hangbai, Li Denghui, Li Mengnan, Pan Gongzhan, Zheng Tonghe, Zhou Feicheng, Zhu Shaoping, Wang Lianfang, Huang Zaoxiong, Lin Kanghou, and others, totaling over a hundred people, attended. First, the total team leader reported the general amount of the second results. Then, Xu Shiying, Li Tingan, Lin Kanghou, and others gave speeches in succession. Finally, Zhu Shaoping, the director of the solicitation section, announced the scores of each team. The details are recorded below:

Report by the Total Team Leader

The total team leader Wu Tiecheng reported, roughly stating that today is the day for the Shanghai City Collection Team of the Chinese Aviation Association to report its second results. In terms of organizations, the achievements this time include: (1) the Shanghai Fresh Meat Industry Association proposed that the association raise 100,000 yuan to purchase an aircraft to be named the "Shanghai Fresh Meat Industry" aircraft; (2) the Guangdong native place association in Shanghai initiated a collection of 100,000 yuan to purchase a fighter plane, which is now underway; (3) the "Shanghai Boy Scout" aircraft planned to be purchased by the ten Shanghai city boy scouts will begin a general mobilization on the 27th. In terms of individuals, the most commendable achievements include: (1) Gu Jiatang 12,000 yuan; (2) Lu Fengzhu 10,450 yuan; (3) Du Yuesheng, Yan Yukun, Lu Zhengbing, Yang Hu, Yang Weiyin, etc., 10,000 yuan each. The total amount has reached over 290,000 yuan. Now we calculate that there is only one month and five days left until the end date. The total amount received in these two collections is still very different from our estimated goal of 2 million yuan. However, the total population of Shanghai is 3 million, and Shanghai is the economic center of the country. All other businesses are in a leading position. This time we are holding the aviation saving the nation movement in Shanghai because we believe that aviation is the most needed weapon in national defense. I think if we unite the enthusiasm of the people of the whole city and the efforts of the team leaders and members of each team, this number of 1 million yuan can definitely be achieved and become an advocate for the whole country. People in Shanghai have a saying, "Merchants don't惜錢, soldiers don't惜命," and another saying, "You only make money when there's a fight." But if you only value money, it's not very useful, because money can't be directly used as a weapon. We must exchange the money for weapons, supply them to the soldiers, and only then can the soldiers take these weapons to kill the enemy, defend the country, and protect the nation.

Lin Kanghou's Speech

Next, Lin Kanghou, in his capacity as the secretary of the Aviation Association, gave a speech to the public, roughly stating that the aviation saving the nation movement we are holding this time is not hoping that the people will donate money and immediately purchase aircraft to go to the front line to kill the enemy. Our intention is to recognize the importance of the position of the aviation industry today, and the aviation industry in our country is still so infantile. Therefore, the people should take the initiative to launch and build aviation. The association now plans to use the donated funds to establish an aeronautical school in Shanghai, and plans to establish a factory to repair various parts inside aircraft. The association deeply believes that this movement did not occur on a momentary impulse, but focuses on the spirit of aviation construction.

Efforts of the Fresh Meat Industry

The Fresh Meat Industry Association of this city voluntarily donated money to purchase the "Shanghai Fresh Meat Industry aircraft." According to the representative of the association at the meeting, the association will stipulate donation methods, and plans that within one year, each store will pay 10 cents for the aviation saving the nation fund for each pig slaughtered, which will be collected by the pig merchants on their behalf. If the money cannot be collected in full within one year, then other methods will be set up to achieve the goal of collecting 100,000 yuan to purchase an aircraft within one year.

Suggestions from Two Organizations

Two Major Proposals for Saving the Nation

The 26th Branch of the First Special District City Federation and the Jiangxi Road Business Community Federation sent an important recommendation letter yesterday to the City Federation and other organizations. Here is the original letter divided into sections.

Rent Contributions for Aviation Funds

The Battle of Shanghai on January 28th, the market strike against resistance, lasted for three months. The most vibrant districts have been devastated. Survivors after the war, the movement to reduce rent can ease the burden on the people. Since the municipal government issued the rent exemption measures, the central district and other areas have not been treated fairly. Fortunately, the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters forwarded the issue to the central government, and the rent reduction measures are being revised. However, it should not be delayed for too long, as it would lose the people's trust. In view of the pressing foreign invasion and the perilous state of the nation, we should learn from the lessons of the Air Force and strive for national salvation. Aviation to save the country, empty talk cannot become a reality. It is necessary to raise considerable funds. Then, regardless of the type of aircraft, it can soar into the sky. Now, the rent for the Shanghai war that has not been waived should be uniformly exempted. The resulting funds should be used as aviation expenses. The matter concerns national salvation, we will do our utmost to follow. But the municipal authorities should lead by example, and hope that the matter will be discussed and submitted to the authorities for implementation.

Economic Sanctions Must Prevent Traitorous Merchants

The Japanese army invaded our territory, using poison gas and air force to wreak havoc on the people. How can the descendants of the Yellow Emperor accept such humiliation? We vow to resist. While our armed comrades are fighting on the battlefield, we unarmed citizens can only implement economic sanctions to express our conscience. However, economic sanctions must stop the source. The only way is to prevent the transportation by traitorous merchants. If the source can be cut off, it is advisable to install secret report boxes for traitorous merchants everywhere, and to request the government to promulgate punitive regulations. Before the government promulgates regulations, the people should automatically be vigilant. This will not only show the national spirit, but also unite us to save the nation. We urge you to discuss and approve it.

Sinking of the Yutong Steamer

Company Seeks Rescue

Crew Reported Safe

The Yutong steamer of Yuda Company ran aground on Qixing Reef outside Xinghua, Fujian, the day before yesterday at about 7 a.m. These details were already noted in yesterday's newspaper. Here are the additional details obtained yesterday.

Naval Department Sends Ship for Protection

The Yuda branch office on Yong'an Street received a telegram the day before yesterday about the accident of the Yutong ship outside Xinghua. The company requested the Shipping Association to telegraph the Shanghai office of the Naval Department and the Fujian Naval Department to send a ship for protection. Yesterday we heard that the Naval Department had already telegraphed nearby patrol ships to rush to protect it.

Insurance Company Salvages

The ship had previously insured a peace insurance with Lianbao Company for 120,000 yuan (yesterday's newspaper mistakenly stated 120,000 taels). The company has now notified Lianbao Company, and the insurance company has contacted the Japanese salvage company yesterday to arrange salvage procedures due to the relationship of responsibility. It is learned that the salvage company has telegraphed the Moji Company and heard that the Oura Maru salvage ship has been designated to go to the scene of the accident to investigate, but the ship will not arrive until next Tuesday.

Yutong's Situation Yesterday

Yesterday morning, Yuda Company received another telegram from the Xinghua agency, which stated that the first and second holds of the ship had been flooded with 1.2 feet of water, and there was still no news of the goods being taken out. It is hoped that there will be no strong winds in the next few days, so it will not capsize. The company then telegraphed to inform them that Japanese ships had been sent from Moji to rescue them.

Crew Not in Danger

The senior crew members of the ship are all Japanese, including the shipowner Sanshen Longxiong, the first mate Marukawa Fuji'erlang, the second mate Chinese (because the name is unknown due to recent change), the engineer Ise Zhongcang, the chief manager Li Wenjin, the second manager He Zhendong, four helmsmen, eight sailors, eight stokers, four oilers, fourteen clerks, and ten servants, a total of fifty-four people. According to the company's news, about a part of the crew has arrived in Xinghua, and it is also said that this Yutong accident, the ship may be unsalvageable, and the crew will not be in danger.

The City Federation will hold tomorrow

National Goods Movement Propaganda

And Fill in the Oath to Not Buy or Sell Enemy Goods

The Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of this city decided at the representatives' meeting the day before yesterday to actively check Japanese goods and carry out the National Goods Movement. The association has now scheduled to publicly promote the National Goods Movement Propaganda Week at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce tomorrow (Monday) at 3 pm, and has formulated a pledge form for stores to not sell or buy enemy goods to be issued to stores in each district to fill in. The oath says, "I, [name], hereby pledge to comply with the instructions of the National Goods Movement Committee of the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of Shanghai, and will strive to promote national goods and never buy or sell enemy goods in the future. If I deliberately violate this pledge and secretly sell enemy goods, I will willingly accept severe punishment to fulfill my duty as a citizen. This pledge is hereby made as proof, and the manager will sign and stamp it."

Patriotic Youth Pan Hongsheng

Not Released After Serving Sentence

His Family Asks Citizens' Association for Assistance

The six patriotic people, Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, Tian Shuiyang, Zhu Erkang, and Xia Zida, were arrested by Gordon Road detectives and sent to court for throwing bombs on Kangnao Road in Shanghai West on November 29th last year to warn Yuanchang Foreign Goods Store. Liu Chongwu was sentenced to seven years in prison, and the other five people, including Pan Hongsheng, were sentenced to two to three months in prison. Among them, Pan Hongsheng has served his sentence and should be released immediately according to law. He is still being detained in the Tilanqiao West Prison. His family is extremely panicked. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District, requesting assistance. Here is the original letter: "Respectfully, my son Pan Hongsheng was arrested by the patrol room on November 29th last year on suspicion of throwing bombs. He was sentenced to three months in prison by the court and has served his sentence according to law, but he has not been released. He is in prison, and the suffering is indescribable. My son was motivated by the patriotic movement and acted out of conscience. Since he has been imprisoned, but has not been released after serving his sentence, what is the purpose? It is contrary to the principles of justice. I earnestly request that your association have compassion on my son, who has been imprisoned for his patriotic actions, and has suffered injustice. I implore you to negotiate with the court quickly and release him to maintain the lives of the people. With great anticipation, I respectfully submit this letter to the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of Shanghai. Respectfully, Pan Shunqing."

US on

Total Far East Trade Volume

丨One-Third Reduction Compared to Last Year丨

According to the Great American Evening News, according to the United States Department of Commerce, the total amount of US trade with the Far East last year was worth US$679,330,000, which is nearly one-third less than the US$995,230,000 in the previous year. From this, it can be seen the impact of the world economic downturn, exchange rate fluctuations, and the sharp decline in the purchasing power of the people in most countries in the Far East. Other factors such as increased tariffs, falling prices, and the instability of the political situation in China and India also play a significant role. Last year, US imports from the Far East were worth US$357,818,000, while the previous year it was US$573,632,000, a decrease of 73% compared to 1929. The value of imports in 1929 was 34% less than the average value between 1915 and 1919. Last year, US exports to the Far East were worth US$321,451,000, a decrease of 23.7% compared to US$425,780,000 in the previous year, and a decrease of 60% compared to 1929. The value of exports in 1929 was 43% less than the average value between 1915 and 1919. From this, it can be seen that the US trade with the Far East was sluggish last year. Last year, US exports to China were worth US$67,052,000, a decrease of 41.7% compared to the previous year. Exports to Japan were worth US$134,537,000, a decrease of 13.6% compared to the previous year. Exports to the Philippines were worth US$44,987,000, a decrease of 8% compared to the previous year.

Nanyang

Resolution of the Tobacco Factory Strike

Satisfactory Results of Yesterday's Interrogation

Four Measures Agreed Upon, Provisional Conclusion

Arrested Workers Released, Entering Factory Tomorrow

According to the National News Agency, a major strike occurred at Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company due to the workers organizing a union office, resulting in the detention of seven workers, which has resulted in a serious situation. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, Party and government organs specially convened an interrogation of both parties at the Social Affairs Bureau. The labor representatives Zhang Zhang and Wu Jiuzhang, and the capital representatives Liang Zhenqing and Chen Deshen were present. The meeting was chaired by Wang Xianqing, director of the Mediation Section of the Third Division of the Social Affairs Bureau, and Zhang Sheng, a member of the Civil Training Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters, attended as an observer. First, the chairman immediately inquired about the circumstances of both parties. The labor representative stated that the company interfered with the organization of the union and illegally instructed the police to detain the workers. The capital representative then stated that the factory did not oppose the workers' union, and it was also possible to negotiate on the proposed conditions according to the procedures. As for the police detention of the workers, the labor side said that it was instructed by the factory, which is absolutely untrue. If the workers do not beat the staff and do not disturb order, they will never be arrested, but they do not know whether the union is a legal organization. The representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters immediately replied that it was indeed approved by the Party Headquarters in accordance with legal procedures. The chairman then said to both parties that today, they will inquire about the beating problem in order to solve it first. As for the proposed conditions and whether the procedures are legal, they will not be discussed for the time being. I hope that the capital side will care for the workers, and the labor side will understand and cooperate with the capital side. The following four measures are proposed, and both parties are requested to accept them: (1) The arrested workers will wait for the court to release them (the Party and government have consulted the court to handle it) (2) The conditions proposed by the labor side will be temporarily withdrawn and submitted to the Municipal Party Headquarters for review and then proposed (3) The capital side's use of force to suppress workers should be revoked immediately (4) The workers should be well-behaved and not be used by others. If the above four points are accommodated by both parties, the strike can be temporarily concluded, and all workers will enter the factory as usual next Monday. After the chairman finished speaking, both parties expressed satisfaction, and the strike came to an end.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Again Requests Exemption

Autumn and Winter House Donations for Jiangwan Last Year

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a letter to the Municipal Government, again requesting exemption from the autumn and winter house donations for Jiangwan last year. The original letter said, "Submitted for request, it is found that the case of the Shanghai war zone requesting exemption from the house donations for the two seasons of autumn and winter in the 21st year was submitted by the association based on the letter from the Wusong sub-office in October last year. After submission, the government approved and instructed that the house donations for the spring and summer seasons in the war zone have been exempted. The request is a general case and is difficult to approve, etc., and the instructions have been followed in separate letters. Now, on the 23rd of this month, the Jiangwan sub-office of the association stated in its letter that after the Shanghai war, 19 towns in Jiangwan were reduced to ashes. After the ceasefire agreement was concluded, merchants returned to their hometowns to clean up the debris, which was in the late summer and autumn. Therefore, the actual resumption of business was mostly at the end of the year, and the municipal government clearly ordered the exemption of taxes and donations, only covering the spring and summer. The merchants in this district have not benefited. On the 18th of this month, the association and the Wusong sub-office jointly presented a letter to the municipal government, and Chen, the clerk, was sent to receive it, and agreed to forward it. However, this case is a fundamental interest of the merchants in the Wusong and Jiangwan districts, and a written request is made again for verification. Please observe the hardships of the merchants in this district and forward it to the municipal government for exemption to maintain the difficulties of the people." According to this, it is found that the city's war zone has stipulated the method of reducing and exempting house donations, originally limited to the spring and summer seasons. However, Jiangwan is the center of the war. In the spring, it was under shelling. In the summer, the ceasefire agreement was just signed. During these two seasons, there was no house donation to speak of. It was not until cleaning up the debris and slowly seeking business resumption that most of them were in autumn and winter. If we rush to order the collection of donations in accordance with the regulations when this remnant breath has just stabilized and the vitality has not recovered, the merchants will not be able to reach it. The request to exempt the house donations for the autumn and winter seasons last year really has the hardship of having no choice, and it seems that it cannot be treated with routine. It is reasonable to submit a request to the government for verification and permission, which is convenient for the public.

Workers from the leaf and tin packaging factories of the Anglo-American Tobacco Company's new factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, clashed the day before yesterday and injured many people. The original letter said, "Respectfully, according to the report of the Fifth District Executive Committee of this association, Shen Baokang, Tang Songlin, Gao Kuiyuan, and other workers from the leaf department of the English and American Tobacco Factory led a crowd to commit murder and beat Zhu Zhaolin, Zhang Aoqi, and other workers from the tin packaging department of the new factory. He has been summoned by the Public Security Bureau, and I sincerely request that you transfer the letter to arrest the murderer and release him." The Arrested Murderer is Sent to the Hospital: Wang Daofu, Yu Chengling, Xu Changfu, Tang Songlin, Shen Baokang, and Ren Zhenxiang, who were suspected of being arrested, were arrested by the Public Security Bureau of the Third District of Pudong and transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Investigation of Injured Workers: Zhu Zhaolin and other nine injured workers were transferred from Tongren Hospital to Fenglinqiao Orthopedic Hospital yesterday morning. (7) Ding Shanhai and Wang Boqing were injured in the head, and Gao Jinyuan was injured in the foot.

Aftermath Relief Association Meeting

The Zhengtayonghe Rubber Workers' Relief Association convened an emergency meeting yesterday at 2 PM. Zhao Maolin chaired the meeting. After formal greetings, the chairman reported on the work done in the past few days and read out the family's request for assistance. Subsequently, Zhou Zitian, representing the families of the Zhengtai victims, and Yan Foxing, a worker from the Zhengtai factory, reported on the situation. The investigator reported on: (1) discrepancies in the number of deaths reported by the factory; (2) inconsistencies in the factory's compensation; (3) the factory's deceptive practices toward the workers; (4) the reasons why the affected families were pressured into accepting meager compensation. Discussions then began, and several resolutions were passed on the spot, as summarized below: (1) Regarding how to handle the case of Zhengtai factory owner Huang Jianqing, who is cunning, disregards human life, and dares to disobey laws and regulations, it was resolved that: A. The authorities should be petitioned to revoke his business license; B. Notices should be sent to business firms in other cities, urging them not to trade with him in the future; C. A letter should be sent to local transportation companies, urging them not to transport his goods; D. A stern warning should be issued. (2) Regarding the issue of how the two factories handled the aftermath carelessly and reported it vaguely to the authorities for record, it was resolved that separate appeals should be submitted to the Party and government, requesting that the record not be approved, and that representatives be appointed to jointly petition with the workers' families. (3) Regarding how to deal with a certain lawyer who illegally resolved the entrustment of some Zhengtai workers, it was resolved that a stern letter of inquiry should be sent. (4) (Omitted). (5) Regarding whether to approve the request from Zhengtai workers and their families to form a crying and appealing group, it was resolved that the request should be approved, and that three to five representatives should be appointed to be responsible for organizing it. The rest is omitted.

Shanghai Municipal Council

Political Views of Council Candidate Lei Wen

| Does Not Advocate for Immediate Tax Increases |

Ten candidates for the Shanghai Municipal Council have successively published their opinions on municipal affairs, which were recorded in this newspaper on the previous two days. Yesterday, American candidate Lei Wen also published his political views, stating roughly that although Shanghai's taxes are very low compared to other similarly prosperous cities around the world, he opposes immediate tax increases during this period of economic recession. He would rather issue public bonds to cover special expenses. The police, fire brigade, and sanitation department should all have their vacancies filled. No more large sums of money should be allocated for the construction of new roads or the extension of old roads in the coming year, but existing roads must be repaired on time and widened and straightened whenever possible. All municipal affairs must be maintained effectively, but at the same time, vigorous efforts must be made to practice economy. A solution to the issue of roads built beyond the concession must be found within the coming year, so that roads can be repaired and the convenience of telephones and water and electricity can be improved.

Shocking News

Poisonous Substances Found in Japanese Goods Shipped to China

Some time ago, newspapers in Wuhan reported that compatriots residing in Japan had found an English letter in the Drunken Weng Pavilion restaurant in Yokohama. The letter stated that the Imperial Japanese Military Medical School had established a Poison China Expedited Drug Research Society to place substances in gauze, cotton textiles, and daily necessities sold in China to spread epidemics. Their intentions are extremely vicious. The translated version of the original letter is as follows: Dear friends, Salerm Laisen. I am currently residing in Osaka and have learned of a most accurate matter, which I present to you for your special attention. Japan's invasion of China is an active and unremitting endeavor. During October 1931, the Imperial Japanese Military Medical School established a Poison China Expedited Drug Research Society. The purpose is to use scientific methods to place all kinds of toxins into necessities for human consumption. Some of the toxins cause permanent infertility (i.e., toxins hidden in clothing materials), while others cause cholera (such as adding such germs into cosmetics or utensils). Their malicious intentions to harm the Chinese people can be seen. However, we who reside in China must also be careful. In addition to my telegraphing the government to alert the people, I hereby inform you. I wish you good health. Sincerely, Jia Maseqi.

Approved by the Public Utilities Bureau

Fare Increase for Chinese Tramways

Starting next month, the first and second class fares will increase by two copper coins.

According to a Shinshi Telegraph Agency local news report, the Nanshi Water and Electricity Company has not increased its fares in the past three years. Recently, due to the depreciation of copper coins, it has become difficult to maintain all expenses. Therefore, it applied to the Public Utilities Bureau for permission to increase fares to maintain operations. It is now learned that the Public Utilities Bureau believes that the application is factual and has approved the company to increase the fares for first and second class by two copper coins each, starting from the first day of next month.

Gang Fight Between Rickshaw Pullers

Using Bricks and Wooden Sticks as Weapons

Resulting in Multiple Injuries on Both Sides

Between Avenue Edward VII and Rue de Hartong and Route Say Zoong in western Shanghai, a major fight broke out yesterday at 10:45 AM between the rickshaw gang and the cart gang. The cause of the fight had been brewing for a long time, but the main reason was still competition for business. Yesterday morning, over a hundred rickshaw pullers gathered near the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Rue de Hartong. When they saw five or six carts working in the direction of Route Say Zoong at around 10 AM, they each grabbed bricks and rushed toward the cart pullers. At the time, there were also forty or fifty cart pullers, each holding bamboo poles to fight back. A chaotic battle ensued, with shouts shaking the sky, disrupting traffic and causing considerable disorder. The melee lasted for about a quarter of an hour. The Jing'an Temple Road police station, having received a report, dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives and police cars to the scene and immediately ordered arrests. Seeing the detectives arrive, the rickshaw pullers scattered, and over thirty people and twenty rickshaws were seized on the spot and taken to the police station for detention. Among the thirty-odd people arrested, nine were injured, but the injuries were minor. However, the fact is that at around 8 AM yesterday morning, the Gongda Freight Automobile Company of Zhoujiaqiao in western Shanghai loaded a large quantity of bricks and tiles from the Zhensou Brick and Tile Company in Caojiadu, intending to transport them to the Yuanhechang yard at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Seymour Road. Unexpectedly, when they were about to reach their destination, they suddenly encountered over a hundred human-powered rickshaws transporting bricks and tiles from the White Railing to the Yongchangtai yard in western Jing'an Temple. When the rickshaw pullers saw the Gongda automobile, they swarmed forward to stop the automobile from unloading. The escorts and drivers of the automobile, seeing the rickshaw pullers obstructing them unreasonably, stepped forward to reason with them. Words quickly escalated into a mutual brawl, resulting in injuries on both sides. Nearby police officers, hearing the commotion, arrived and arrested everyone involved, taking them to the police station. The police chief ordered them to reconcile outside, but the Gongda Freight Automobile Company immediately reported the incident to the Shanghai Freight Automobile Industry Association and hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Gu Rumei, Hu Xiaodazi, and other rickshaw pullers who instigated the violence.

Miao Qinghe

Death by Eating Pufferfish Roe

Whole Body Numb, Jumping Like Thunder

Seized Up Like Electrocution, Died Untreated

Miao Qinghe, a 45-year-old man from Ningbo, lived at No. 161 Dengtuo Road and sold spiced beans for a living. He usually enjoyed a drink. At around 10 AM the day before yesterday, Miao bought two large pieces of pufferfish roe at the market and took them home. After cooking them, he used them as snacks to go with his wine, eating half of the roe. Initially, he did not feel anything, but unexpectedly, at around 6 PM, Miao suddenly became numb all over, jumping like thunder, as if he had been electrocuted. His wife, Zhu, was frightened and panicked when she saw this and immediately sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He suddenly died at around 11 PM. According to the hospital doctor's diagnosis, it was indeed caused by eating too much pufferfish roe. The hospital then reported it to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The body was then taken to the Pielun Road autopsy station. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court was requested to appoint Prosecutor Guo Wei, forensic doctor Zhang Yan, and clerk Wang Zuyi to go to the station to examine the body. Taking the bench, he questioned the deceased's wife, Miao Zhu, who testified, "My husband bought sorghum wine and pufferfish roe from the market that day and told me to cook it for him to eat. I and others do not like to drink wine, so only he ate it alone. But I did not know that eating this product could cause death, so I did not stop him at the time," and so on. After hearing the testimony, Guo Jun ordered the examination to confirm that the deceased, Miao Qinghe, had indeed died from poisoning after eating pufferfish roe. The body was handed over to his wife, Miao Zhu, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial, pending further investigation and verification.

For the Compensation of One Dozen Stockings

Female Worker Hangs Herself in Resentment

| Jiang Genxiong Died a Pitiable Death |

Jiang Guisheng, a porter at a coal store who hailed from Gaoyou, lived in a side room at No. 34 Laoxiaopilu Lane in Nanshi. His wife, Jiang Shen, rowed a small boat in the Huangpu River. They had a total of five children. Their eldest daughter, Jiang Jindi, was married in the Zhonghua Road area of Xiaoximen. The family also included a second daughter named Genxiong, who was eighteen years old. Life was difficult for the family. Since the eldest daughter worked at the Jiucheng Stocking Factory on Penglai Road, she took her younger sister Genxiong there to learn the trade last winter. She had already completed her apprenticeship and was now working at the factory. On the 23rd of this month, Jiang Genxiong was ordered to pay compensation by the factory because the stockings she wove were too sparse.

Robbery to Buy Clothes

Store Clerk Detects and Arrests

Four Male and Female Thieves Arrested

Handguns, Bullets, and Stolen Goods Seized

On the afternoon of the 23rd of this month, at 8:30 PM, the Wanyuanxin Sauce Garden opened by Zhang Ming, a resident of Zhapu, at No. 44 Houjie Xiejiaodong Lane, Manufacturing Bureau Road, Nanshi, was robbed. Details were recorded in this newspaper yesterday. It is now learned that the robbers were caught on the previous two days, and handguns, bullets, and stolen goods were seized. Details are listed below.

Thieves Hide Out The male and female robbers fled to the Jiuhua Hotel at No. 60 Jinshouli, Shandong Road, W马 Road, in the Public Concession with the stolen goods. They rented rooms 28 and 34, divided the loot, and converted the clothes and gold jewelry into cash.

Buying Clothes One of the robbers, wearing a gray western-style raincoat over a bronze-colored silk robe, and a female robber, wearing striped clothes, went to the Hongfu Clothing Store at the intersection of Fujian Road (i.e., Shilu) and L马 Road at 1:45 PM the day before yesterday to buy clothes. They were greeted by the store clerk, Ren Binlai, who showed them a small cotton jacket, but because the quality was not good, they argued with Ren Binlai.

Clerk Detects the Deception The Hongfu Clothing Store had a clerk from Zhapu named Lu Changlin, who lived upstairs from Zhang Ming's Wanyuanxin Sauce Garden at No. 44 Houjie Xiejiaodong Lane, Manufacturing Bureau Road, Nanshi, which was also robbed. At the time, Lu was standing next to the counter, carefully looking at the customers, and they looked very much like the robbers. He then heard them speaking with a Jiangbei accent and saw that the raincoat had a lot of mud on the back.

Details of the Capture Lu Changlin saw that the robbers did not buy the clothes and turned to leave, so he followed them to Jinshouli Lane, W马 Road, Shandong Road. The male and female robbers then went out again and passed the entrance of the Gongtai Clothing Store on S马 Road, Fujian Road. Lu Changlin then called out to Chinese constable No. 530 there. The male robber was arrested on the spot, and the female robber escaped from the crowd.

Taken Back for Interrogation Detectives from the Lao Zha Police Station interrogated them briefly. Because the incident occurred in the Chinese area, they notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Detective Team Leader Lu Ying dispatched Wu Xiufeng, the leader of the team stationed in the Second District, with a document to take the robber back to the team for interrogation. The robber confessed, "Zhu Jinshan, 34 years old, from Qingjiang, admits to colluding with others to commit robbery with guns." Stolen goods were found on him. He also confessed the hiding place of his accomplices.

Continued Arrest of Accomplices After reviewing the confession, Lu Ying immediately dispatched detective leaders Zhou Peisan and detectives Wu Zuorong and Lu Zhenyuan to escort the Zhu suspect to the concession to meet with Chinese and foreign detectives from the police station. They went to rooms 28 and 34 of the Jiuhua Hotel at No. 60 Jinshouli, W马 Road, Shandong Road, and arrested two robbers: Liu Youcai, 40 years old, from Huai'an, and the female robber, Shen Yueshi, 34 years old, from Huai'an. Stolen cash totaling 30 yuan, 84 jiao in double coins, and 24 jiao in single coins, 23 pawn tickets, and leather clothing and other items were seized on the spot.

Strict Interrogation During the interrogation of the robbers, the team summoned the victims to the team to identify the robbers, who were confirmed to be them. The robbers also confessed to using the stolen goods and confessed that two handguns were hidden in the Ma Carriage Company at No. 151 Meixie Road in Nanshi. Lu sent the original team of detectives to go to the address with police officers from the Second District at around 12:00 PM yesterday to search and seize two handguns and twelve bullets. They also arrested Feng Wangshi, a 20-year-old woman from Qingjiang, and took her to the team for detention and interrogation. It is reported that the detectives will go to the various pawnshops today to track down the stolen goods and continue to arrest the remaining fugitives. They are temporarily being held in the team.

Jumping into the Huangpu River Afraid of the Cold

Young Lin Wenfu Was Fortunately Saved

At around 5 PM the day before yesterday, a young man hired a No. 360 sampan at the Zhaofeng Road Wharf in Hongkou, claiming that he was crossing to Pudong. The sampan operator, Lin Xingru, immediately cast off and rowed towards the opposite bank. Unexpectedly, when he reached the middle of the river, the young man suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. His body sank and then floated up again. The sampan operator was shocked and used a bamboo pole to try to save him. The young man grabbed the bamboo pole and was pulled back onto the boat. He was then sent to the Customs Water Police Station. He identified himself as Lin Wenfu, 18 years old, from Fujian. He refused to reveal the reason for his suicide attempt. When police officers asked why he grabbed the pole to get back on the boat if he wanted to commit suicide, his answer was quite amusing. He claimed that the water in the Huangpu River was very cold and he could not bear it, so it was not worth dying. Those who heard this were amused. When asked where he lived and whether he had any relatives or friends in Shanghai, he replied that he had no address, only a friend named Peng Demao who lived in the Xinkaihe area. The police station then sent Detective Huang Songsheng to the address to summon his friend to come and take him back.

Eastern Shanghai District

Emergency Meeting on Refusal to Cut Off Water

| Residents in the Water Cut-off Area Drink Unclean Water and 19 Became Ill |

The Eastern Shanghai District Citizens' Committee for Refusing to Cut Off Water held an emergency meeting yesterday at 5 PM to discuss solutions, based on reports from residents in the water cut-off area. Chairman Qiu Jialiang chaired the meeting, and the following resolutions were passed: Representatives of residents in flat houses along the corner of Qiwupu Road and Baikai'er Road came to the meeting and claimed that after the water company closed the main switch, the landlord prohibited tenants from opening it. If they opened it without permission, they were threatened with the renovation of the house. Moreover, there were no public water hydrants nearby, so they had no way to get water. They could only draw water from the natural well behind the house. The well water was extremely muddy and very unsanitary, causing 19 residents there to become ill. They requested assistance from the committee. The committee believed the situation was serious and immediately sent a letter to the Real Estate Industry Association, urgently warning the landlord to protect people's lives and actively appealing to various organizations for assistance. The meeting adjourned at 7 PM.

The Truth Is Unclear

Empty Wooden Box Scam

Only One of the 26 Wooden Boxes Contained Rayon

The Other 25 Boxes Contained Wood Shavings and Brick Mud

The Purpose Was to Switch Goods and Defraud Customs

According to Song Bingzheng and Ye Yuxi, drug enforcement detectives, and Xu Guirong, a detective, from the Drug Enforcement Group of the Public Concession Police Department, there was a report that prohibited drugs were hidden in the Wufeng Customs Brokerage at No. 41 Yuegui Lane, Guangdong Road. The chief reported it and applied to the First Special District Local Court for a search warrant. They went to the customs brokerage at 2:30 PM the day before yesterday to conduct a search. They found 26 wooden boxes. The detectives, wanting to know what kind of items were stored in the boxes, opened and inspected each box. Unexpectedly, 25 of the boxes contained worthless items such as wood shavings and brick mud. Only one box contained rayon. The detectives were puzzled by their purpose. They arrested four people with close ties to the wooden boxes: Qian Hegeng from Yong, Xu Jingxiang, Qi Bingwen from Changzhou, and Monk Wang from Wuxi. They also took the wooden boxes back to the police station. Under investigation, it was learned that the purpose of preparing the wooden boxes was to defraud customs of goods. The method of deception was very thorough and rarely revealed any flaws, so it was usually not easy to solve the case. It is now known that to deceive and obtain certain goods, they would first prepare wooden boxes with the same decoration as the goods and report them to customs for shipment. When the goods left the customs warehouse, they would take the opportunity to switch them, replacing the real goods with fake ones. What other tricks they used are still under investigation by the detectives. The full story will be revealed in the future. Yesterday morning, the police sent Qian and the other four to the First Special Court. Judge Huang Risheng questioned them. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, and Zhang Shizhu, stated that they were prosecuting the four defendants for fraud. However, how the defendants were defrauding in this case is still under detailed investigation and should be adjourned to a later date. Judge Chen briefly questioned each defendant and ordered them to be detained pending further investigation.

The Changshu woman, Shi Chen, and her daughter, Jinghua, jointly hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit with the Second Special District Court, accusing Wu Huaichun, a Suzhou native living at No. 45, Jiwu Lane, West Gate Road, of raping her fourteen-year-old daughter, Lingyu, last summer, causing her to become ill and die. Verification of the Tragic Death of Du Nanxi

丨The Body is Handed Over to Zhong Bojie for Funeral Arrangements丨

Du Nanxi, a native of Sichuan, 26 years old, formerly studied in the Municipal Administration Department of Fudan University in Jiangwan. On the 21st of this month, he came to Shanghai by plane from Hankou and stayed at Fudan University, planning to marry his fiancée, Ding Yandao, who is currently working in the Education Bureau of Jinshan Zhu Jing, in Shanghai. On the morning of the day before yesterday, Du came to Shanghai from the school. At 8:30 in the morning, he was shot and assassinated in front of No. 54, Puqing Lane, Malang Road, in the French Concession, and died from head injuries. The police station transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall autopsy room and sent detectives to the school to investigate. Zhang Rong, a friend of the deceased, came to Shanghai to identify the situation, which has been detailed in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Section of the French Concession Police Department reported to the Second Special District Court, requesting Prosecutor Deng Baosun to come to the place with a forensic doctor and clerk to examine the body. According to Detective Wang Licheng's report on the case, Zhang Rong, a classmate and fellow villager of the deceased, stated that the deceased left the school for Shanghai yesterday morning and did not know how he was assassinated. He and the deceased were from the same hometown and had been classmates for a long time. He knew his character and could guarantee that he had no political affiliations. He came to Shanghai this time to get married. After arriving in Shanghai, he sent a letter to his fiancée, Ms. Ding. Yesterday at noon, the school received a reply from Ding, inviting the deceased to go to Zhu Jing. However, he did not know if he had any enemies. Now he has a relative, Zhong Bojie, at the China Public School, and he has notified him. The body can be taken care of by Zhong, etc. However, Zhong had not arrived at the time of the autopsy. The official then ordered that the body of Du Nanxi was indeed shot and killed, and the body was allowed to be taken care of by Zhong Bojie. The police were ordered to investigate and apprehend the murderer. After the autopsy, Zhong arrived and filled out a guarantee for claiming the body before transporting the body to the China Funeral Home for coffin arrangements.

New Bride

Holding a Kitchen Knife to Chop at the Mother-in-Law's Head

Romantic by Nature... Unaccustomed to Being a Wife

Transgressing Moral Standards... Sent to the Authorities for Investigation

Zhang Ji, a villager in Zhengang Township, the Third District of Shanghai County, comes from a family of modest means and has two sons, Fangsheng and Xiangsheng. Her husband died many years ago, and she relies on farming and weaving for a living. The elder son, Fangsheng, has been married for six years, and the younger son, Xiangsheng, was engaged to Da Jin, the daughter of Weng Qin, from the same township, through the introduction of Sun Guisheng when he was young. On the twenty-second day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year, Zhang Ji married Xiangsheng to complete the family. Unexpectedly, the wedding sedan was met with refusal. By midnight, the bride had not yet boarded the sedan. After receiving the news, Zhang Ji asked the township head, Jin Diangeng, to mediate. Only then was Da Jin brought home for the wedding on the morning of the next day. Unexpectedly, one wave had just subsided, and another rose. On the second day of the marriage, Xiangsheng's mother-in-law, Weng Qin, actually brought several armed men to Zhang's house to take Da Jin back. Later, local impartial people came forward to mediate, and the matter was finally resolved. According to Da Jin's usual behavior, she is very romantic and unaccustomed to being a wife. After six days in the same room, she returned home. At that time, it happened to be the local welcoming the gods festival. Da Jin went out and returned with her young boyfriend. Although Zhang Ji and Xiangsheng heard about it, they could not stop it. Yesterday, Zhang Ji went to Weng Qin's house to bring the new bride home to help with everything as the farm work was getting busy and to fulfill her wish of having a grandson as soon as possible. Unexpectedly, Da Jin, with her fierce and barbaric nature, grabbed a kitchen knife and chopped at her mother-in-law's head several times, causing Zhang Ji's face to be covered with blood and tears, and she fell to the ground in extreme pain. Neighbors came to help her home. Zhang's family and the elders of the village were indignant. Zhang Ji, having been chopped by the knife of her daughter-in-law, a matter that transgressed moral standards, reported the incident to the Zhuanqiao Police Station of the Third Public Security Bureau under its jurisdiction. After questioning by Chief Zhu, she was sent to the Third Public Security Bureau because the case concerned harm to a senior relative, and then sent to the County Government for legal investigation.

Letter

To the Editor: The Shenbao, Xinwenbao, and Chengbao have reported for days that our bureau has dismissed a large number of staff and employees, and at the same time, it has newly appointed a large number of staff and employees. Although our bureau has repeatedly received orders from the Ministry of Railways to strictly reduce staff and reduce administration due to the financial difficulties of the two railways, the dismissal of the staff this time is not entirely based on austerity. In fact, some of them have been involved in corruption, or have weak knowledge and abilities, or are incompetent, or do not observe discipline. After careful investigation by the responsible officials, they had to be dismissed separately in order to rectify the situation. The newly appointed employees are mostly transferred from the Ministry of Railways and other departments. For example, Secretary Xiao Weiguo, Deputy Director of the General Affairs Department Yuan Boyang, Director of the Materials Department Sun Xuexiu, and Director of the Transportation Division Wang Yunyuan are all members of the Ministry. Director of the General Affairs Department Mo Heng is the technician and section chief of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, and Section Chief of the General Affairs Section Cao Shengzhi is the technician of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and concurrently the Deputy Director of the Ferry General Administration. They all have considerable positions and salaries, or still retain their original positions, so our bureau wants to rely on them and cannot but give them preferential treatment. Moreover, according to the regulations of the Ministry of Railways, the appointment and dismissal of staff and employees in our bureau, directors, deputy directors, secretaries, section chiefs, and employees of the same level are directly appointed by the Ministry, and the salaries of other staff and employees reaching one hundred yuan must be approved by the Ministry of Railways for appointment. In addition, if the public expenses paid reach ten yuan, it must also be approved by the Ministry. In addition, the appointment and dismissal of police officers in the police department are directly managed by the Railway Police Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Railways. The director of the bureau cannot interfere. Only the staff and employees whose salaries are less than one hundred yuan can the director of the bureau freely appoint and dismiss. Therefore, the director of the Lianglu Bureau's employment rights are subject to strict restrictions. The staff who have been dismissed now know this procedure, but they generally say that the director dismissed 61 old employees and appointed 57 new employees, hoping to stir up gossip from all sides. This alone proves what kind of people they are. Taking the so-called dismissal of 61 old employees, only 22 of them were directly dismissed by the bureau. 28 were directly approved by the Ministry for dismissal. The remaining 11 were either resigned, dismissed by the police department, or even fabricated. Furthermore, among the so-called 57 newly appointed personnel, only 12 were directly appointed by the bureau, and 24 were directly appointed by the Ministry. The remaining 21 were either promoted from existing employees, appointed by the police department, or even fabricated. Furthermore, the Materials Department and the General Affairs Department's General Affairs Section are the only ones with more changes, precisely because these two parts are the hotbeds of corruption. Therefore, the Ministry specifically transferred Technician Sun Xuexiu to be the Director of the Materials Department and borrowed Technician Cao Shengzhi from the Shanghai Municipal Government to be the Section Chief of the General Affairs Section, ordering them to be responsible for sorting out the situation. There is no major change in other departments such as the General Affairs Department's Document Section. Wu Xiwei, the Section Chief of the Document Section, was promoted from the staff of the Industry Section. As for the pension savings, unless they are dismissed or have unfinished business in office, once the responsible official reports it, the Ministry of Railways specifically appoints the road inspector to audit it and confirm that there are no errors, and the accounting department will allocate it. The director of the bureau cannot arbitrarily issue or withhold it. Therefore, various parties have inquired about this matter to our bureau, and we cannot answer each one in detail. Therefore, we have specifically stated the facts in a nutshell, and we hope that your newspaper will publish this letter to clarify the truth. Sincerely, The Jinghu-Huning and Huning-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, March 25th.

Reader Advisor

Boy Scouts and the "New Mission"

丨Letter from Mr. You Cheng of this Port丨

Since your esteemed newspaper began publishing the "Readers' Mailbox," the issues discussed have been numerous. However, there seems to be a lack of discussion regarding group activities. I am not talented, but I respectfully present the issue of the Boy Scout movement for readers to study and ask for space to express my humble opinions as follows.

Boy Scout education is flourishing today like bamboo shoots after rain. The leading organization should be fully sound to avoid repeating the mistakes of the past, which lacked organization. During the January 28th Incident last year, the Shanghai Boy Scout Council was at the forefront, resolutely summoning the heads and trainers of Boy Scout troops in the city to face the national crisis. They organized a battlefield service corps, participating in the resistance against Japan at the front lines, rescuing victims in the rear, and serving in hospitals and shelters for wounded soldiers. Their work was indeed precise, brave, and diligent, demonstrating that Chinese youth truly bear a significant new mission of carrying on the past and opening up the future.

According to the principles of Boy Scout training, the focus of their spirit, the soundness of their bodies and minds, and their courageous, sacrificial, and sincere willpower are worthy of being models for Chinese youth. When we further observe the twelve Boy Scout laws – "Honest, loyal, helpful, friendly, courteous, kind, obedient, cheerful, thrifty, brave, clean, and civic-minded" – we gain a deeper understanding of the inherent character of the Boy Scouts and their spirit of wisdom, benevolence, and courage. These twelve laws are the only effective remedy for the youth of China. In terms of individuals, they cultivate talented individuals who are noble, physically sound, and knowledgeable. In terms of the nation, society, and humanity, they promote mutual assistance, peace, and universal love, gradually approaching the realization of a world of the people, by the people, and for the people. This further proves that Boy Scout training is an important element in saving the nation and is a formidable enemy of romanticism, frivolity, timidity, and melancholy. Therefore, the cultivation of such excellent youth naturally depends on talented individuals with experience, knowledge, and loyalty to take responsibility for molding them. Conversely, if there is a lack of sufficient experience and knowledge, and if the scum of society hastily and perfunctorily seek fame and praise by training these Boy Scouts, the result will only lead to the youth becoming undisciplined and impractical, causing profound harm... (End)

Answer: Your letter discusses the issue of Boy Scouts. However, more than ten years ago, as I served in the education field, I personally founded a Boy Scout troop. At that time, for the establishment ceremony of the Boy Scouts, everyone wanted me to write an introduction. Therefore, I had briefly investigated the history and social relations of the Boy Scouts. Today, I take this opportunity to share my current opinions on the Boy Scouts themselves. However, I must first declare that these are my personal opinions and not some "absolutely indisputable" theory. (1) I remember the origin and reasoning behind Boy Scouts: There was an Englishman (whether he was a military officer, a journalist, or a traveler, I don't remember) who saw in an African colony that the lives of the black soldiers in the army were very arduous, simply unbearable for white people, but the black people were at ease. The Englishman thought: If there is a war between England and the colony, that is to say, the colony rises up in resistance and England goes to suppress it, the English people, used to comfort, may not be confident of victory. So, after returning to England, he created an organization specifically to train young students in hardship and provide basic military training. Before long, this organization spread throughout the country and the world. This is the brief history of the so-called "Boy Scouts." Its initial purpose was only to organize a generation of youth to prepare for the armed suppression of colonial rebellions, the violent foundation of so-called "suppression of counter-revolution." (2) Boy Scouts are not a force in our Chinese patriotic youth's revolutionary war against Japanese imperialism. The Boy Scout uniforms are very neat, and during the war, they "rescue victims in the rear and serve on the battlefield," and that is all. However, the Chinese youth in our eyes are not like this. Our patriotic youth should take up arms themselves and fight to the death with Japanese imperialists and their running dogs, the traitors. However, the current Boy Scouts cannot do this kind of struggle. (3) The so-called creeds of the Boy Scouts, as you mentioned: "Honest, loyal, helpful, friendly, courteous, kind, obedient, cheerful, thrifty, brave, clean, and civic-minded," etc., are all abstract, intangible dogmas, just like the "propriety, justice, integrity, and shame" advocated by celebrities today, not concrete and actionable programs for our survival as a nation. The so-called "loyalty" is naturally copied from the ancient ministers' saying, "Advance in thought, exhaust loyalty; retreat in thought, make up for mistakes." But who should we be loyal to now? The so-called "obedience," who should we obey? And how should we fulfill loyalty? What are the standards for obedience? If you are working under a traitor, should you be loyal to him? Should you obey him? In this way, only simple-minded youth are created to be tools for a few people, which is truly undesirable. (4) Currently, I believe that truly patriotic youth should "rise up as a separate force" to organize a widespread and great armed mobilization group, or simply name it "Chinese Youth Anti-Japanese National Salvation Corps." As long as they are patriotic youth, whether they are students, young clerks, young workers, or young farmers, as long as they sincerely dedicate themselves to this arduous struggle of resisting Japan and saving the nation, they are qualified to join. Its program should be approximately as follows: (1) Use your own brain, stand on the position of the vast majority of the people to think about everything, analyze everything, and study everything. (2) To be loyal, you should only be loyal to the country protected by the vast majority, and only be loyal to the revolutionary war against Japanese imperialism. To obey, you should only obey the organizations trusted by the revolutionary masses who protect the country and resist Japan. (3) Unite the vast majority of youth in the country to resist Japan with arms. (4) Universally implement military training: mechanical, chemical, and tactical. (5) Demand that the government issue weapons. (6) Undertake compulsory education for the majority of the poor, lecturing on the causes, situation, relationship, results, and responsibilities of the Chinese-Japanese war. (7) Study methods of resisting Japan and help the general public organize various anti-Japanese groups. (8) Lecture to the public on the prevention of poison gas and other necessary knowledge and skills that the general public should have during wartime, such as fire prevention, first aid, communication, stretchers, etc. (9) Should be deeply aware that only when the people of the whole country spontaneously and unitedly unite to become the main force in resisting Japan and take on the mission of resisting Japan will the resistance have active and real consciousness and hope. If they are merely weakly waving flags and shouting slogans in the rear, relying solely on a few soldiers to compete with Japan, not only will they not resolutely fight to the end, but even if they do fight to the end, they will only leave a tragic page in history! As for the Shanghai Boy Scouts' service on the battlefield in the past two years, they have made some contributions. This is not due to the effectiveness of the Boy Scouts but the result of a little national consciousness driving the Chinese people. To fulfill this little bit of obligation is not something only the Boy Scouts can do; ordinary young students can also do it. If you conclude from this that "Chinese youth truly bear a significant new mission of carrying on the past and opening up the future," are you not taking things too lightly? And what is the so-called carrying on and opening up, what exactly will be carried on and what will be opened up? Where is the so-called "new mission"? May I ask丨

Education News

Important News

Director Zhou Fo Hai of the Jiangsu Education Department

Inspects Education in Southern Jiangsu (4)

Loves the Children's Lively Joint Photo

Hopes the Education Community Will Fulfill Responsibilities with Earnest Instructions

(Special Dispatch from Changzhou) This morning (the 24th) at 8:00 AM, Director Zhou Fo Hai of the Jiangsu Education Department, accompanied by Section Chief Chen Xifang of the Second Section, Section Chief Xiang Jutan of the Third Section, Chief Editor Yi Junzuo, and others, first went to the County-run Changzhou Women's Normal School for inspection. They observed lessons in Chinese Literature and History of the Second Normal, Chinese Language Practice of the Third Normal, Trigonometry of the First Normal, Botany and Chinese Language of the First Junior High A and B Groups, Algebra and Party Principles of the Second Junior High A and B Groups, Chinese Language of the Third Junior High, and Civics of the Remedial Class. In addition to inquiring about the school's administration and instruction, and providing detailed guidance, he inquired in detail about whether the points indicated by Inspector Jin of the Education Department had been improved. He then went to the affiliated elementary school to inspect the lessons. He paid close attention to children's extracurricular activities, student performance, and school administration. Seeing that the children were lively and lovely, he took a group photo with them. He then went to Xinfangqiao Elementary School and Dongmen Elementary School for inspection. After lunch, he went to Juqian Street Elementary School. The school has a total of nineteen classes and more than 1,400 students, which is rare among elementary schools in Jiangsu Province. Director Zhou and others inspected each class. He believed that the school's method of teachers observing and studying each other could be promoted. He then went to Mi Duqiao and Weaving Workshop two elementary schools, and Fang Hui Women's Middle School for inspection. At 5:30 PM, he returned to his residence to rest. After dinner at 6:00 PM, he went to the County Party Headquarters to give instructions to the entire city's education community. More than 200 people attended. The speech lasted for two hours. The content was divided into one part: (1) General comments on the inspection of Wujin's education, (2) the important responsibilities that the Wujin education community should bear, (3) how educational service personnel can be considered to have fulfilled their responsibilities. It was also divided into two points: (A) Reporting on the Education Department's facilities, (B) Hoping that everyone would cooperate and give full play to their abilities. The listeners were all moved and inspired. The County Party Headquarters has a broadcasting machine, so this speech can be broadcast to the entire Wujin County and Wuxi, etc. (Sent on March 24)

Presidents of Private Middle Schools in Beijing

Petition Again for Unified Examination

The Social Affairs Bureau Should Quickly Formulate Special Measures

Eight presidents or representatives of more than ten registered private middle schools in Beijing, including Yao Wencai, went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on the afternoon of the 24th to petition for the unified examination. Director Wang Chongzhi received them. Because this matter needs to be formulated by the Ministry of Education in order to be implemented, the representatives went to the Ministry of Education at 5:00 PM. Division Chief Gu Yinting received them. The representatives said that after the Ministry of Education announced the unified examination measures, various provinces have special circumstances that can be remedied. Now, Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have already held presidents' meetings to propose measures, and the Education Departments have detailed various regulations, but Beijing has not yet made any plans. The unified examination is approaching soon, so it is necessary to formulate regulations as soon as possible. What we request is: (1) Beijing should quickly organize an examination committee for this matter, so that practical educators can contribute appropriate opinions to the committee, and the selection of committee members should pay attention to the talents of the Beijing education community, so as to avoid separation. (2) The scope and standards of the examination should be based on the actual situation of each school. Because the new curriculum standards were only recently announced, the levels of the schools are very uneven. During the transition period, there should be a compromise remedy. (3) The scoring method should consider the overall situation and reduce the standard of passing scores separately, and the usual grades should also be stipulated to account for a certain percentage of the unified examination scores, so as not to completely obliterate the usual grades due to the length of one day. Division Chief Gu said that this matter must be formulated by the Beijing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau itself. The Ministry of Education had previously meant in a general meeting that it could be changed due to special circumstances. He agreed to urge the Social Affairs Bureau to formulate the unified examination measures as soon as possible in a private capacity and report them to the Ministry for review.

The Ministry of Education Announces

Regulations of the Mass Education Committee

(Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education announced fourteen articles of the Regulations of the Mass Education Committee. The main purpose is to assist the Ministry in planning and promoting mass education affairs nationwide. The Chief and Section Chief of the Social Education Division of the Ministry of Education, and one Counselor and Inspector appointed by the Ministry of Education, are ex officio members. Three members from the Central Party Headquarters, two members from the Ministry of Interior, and four to eight mass education experts and enthusiasts are hired as members. There are five standing committee members, one chief secretary, and several secretaries, who are concurrently held by members appointed by the Minister. A full meeting is held every six months, and a standing committee meeting is held every month. When necessary, various specialized committees may be established or representative meetings of mass education committees from various provinces and cities may be convened.
